Design Manual for Roads and Bridges
Highway Structures & Bridges
Design
CD 350
The design of highway structures
(formerly BD 100/16, BA 57/01, BD 57/01, IAN 124/11)
Version 1.0.0
Summary
This document contains requirements, advice and guidance of the Overseeing Organisation for
the design of highway structures.
Feedback and Enquiries
Users of this document are encouraged to raise any enquiries and/or provide feedback on the content and usage of
this document to the dedicated National Highways team. The online feedback form for all enquiries and feedback
can be accessed at: www.standardsforhighways.co.uk/feedback.
This is a controlled document.
Downloaded from https://www.standardsforhighways.co.uk on 12-Nov-2025, CD 350 Version 1.0.0, published: 30-Sep-2025

Foreword
Publishing information
This document is published by National Highways.
This document supersedes CD 350 version 0.0.0, which is withdrawn.
Contractual and legal considerations
This document forms part of the works specification. It does not purport to include all the necessary
provisions of a contract. Users are responsible for applying all appropriate documents applicable to
their contract.

CD 350 Version 1.0.0
Introduction
Introduction
Background
This document gives requirements, advice and guidance of the Overseeing Organisation on the use of
Eurocodes for the design of highway structures (including any associated geotechnical works, but not
including approach embankments or ground bearing temporary works) and aspects of execution
relevant to the design.
Durability is a key issue throughout the design, detailing and construction phases of highway
structures. Whilst the control of materials and quality of construction is achieved through standards and
procedures, historically the lack of attention to the durability aspect of design has resulted in a
premature loss of serviceability in many highway structures. It has been found that the durability of
many bridges in the Overseeing Organisations' stock has been limited by decisions made at the design
stage in relation to the bridge configuration and the choice of details. These decisions were often
limited to a design philosophy in which minimising the initial capital cost was paramount.
This document aims to promote the concept of design for durability, thereby shifting the emphasis to a
lowest whole life cost design philosophy. It gives requirements and advice to be used in conjunction
with current design standards to improve the durability of highway structures and minimise future
maintenance to avoid disruption.
The document has been amended in response to the update of the Manual of Contract Documents for
Highway Works (MCHW), to ensure that design requirements previously in the Specification for
Highway Works / Notes for Guidance have been transferred to the Design Manual for Roads and
Bridges (DMRB).
Assumptions made in the preparation of this document
The assumptions made in GG 101 [Ref 52.N] apply to this document.

Terms and definitions
Terms and definitions
Terms
Term
Definition
Application Rules
As defined in BS EN 1990 [Ref 43.N]
Approval In Principle
As defined in CG 300 [Ref 94.N]
Category
As defined in CG 300 [Ref 94.N]
Departure from standard
Criterion, which departs from, or is an aspect not covered by, the
standards contained in the Technical Approval Schedule, the
DMRB or project specific requirements
Designated standard
A designated standard is a standard, developed by consensus,
which is recognised by government in part or in full by publishing
its reference on GOV.UK in a formal notice of publication.
Designer record
Used to record decisions that affect the design of the permanent
works
Eurocodes
As defined in BS EN 1990 [Ref 43.N]
European Assessment
Document
A harmonised technical specification for construction products
developed by the European Organisation for Technical
Assessment (EOTA) for cases where a product is not fully
covered by harmonised European standards. European
Assessment Documents are the basis for issuing European
Technical Assessments
Execution
As defined in BS EN 1990 [Ref 43.N]
Harmonised standard
A European standard developed by a recognised European
Standards Organisation: CEN, CENELEC, or ETSI and has been
cited in the Official Journal of the European Union.
Manufacturers, other economic operators, or conformity
assessment bodies can use harmonised standards to
demonstrate that products, services, or processes comply with
relevant EU legislation.
Minor structure
As defined in CD 354 [Ref 18.N]
National Annex
As defined in BS EN 1990 [Ref 43.N]
Nationally Determined Parameter
As defined in BS EN 1990 [Ref 43.N]
Principles
As defined in BS EN 1990 [Ref 43.N]
Published Documents
For the purpose of this document, Published Documents contain
Non-Contradictory Complementary Information (NCCI) to assist
in the application of Eurocode Principles.
Technical Approval Authority
As defined in CG 300 [Ref 94.N]

1. Scope
1.
Scope
Aspects covered
1.1
The requirements set out in this document shall be adopted for the design of highway structures in
concrete, steel and composite concrete steel, masonry, timber and aluminium.
Implementation
1.2
This document shall be implemented forthwith on all schemes involving the design of concrete, steel
and concrete composite, steel, masonry, timber and aluminium structures on the Overseeing
Organisations' motorway and all-purpose trunk roads according to the implementation requirements of
GG 101 [Ref 52.N].
Use of GG 101
1.3
The requirements contained in GG 101 [Ref 52.N]] shall be followed in respect of activities covered by
this document.
11

2. General design requirements
2.
General design requirements
General
2.1
Eurocodes shall be used for the design of new highway structures including any associated
geotechnical works, but not including approach embankments or ground bearing temporary works.
2.2
Where particular clauses within the DMRB documents are in conflict with the Eurocodes, designated
standards, harmonised standards, UK Assessment Documents (UKAD) or European Assessment
Documents (EAD), these clauses shall not be used.
2.2.1
Conflicting DMRB clauses should be reported to the Overseeing Organisation.
2.3
For structures not fully covered by the Eurocode Application Rules, additional design rules including
values of partial factors, combination factors and values and configurations of actions shall be
determined for the individual project, in accordance with the relevant principles given in BS EN 1990
[Ref 43.N].
NOTE
Structures not fully covered by the application rules in the Eurocodes can include special types of
structures such as moveable bridges or bridges carrying both road and rail/light rail traffic.
2.3.1
Eurocodes may be applied, with agreement from the Overseeing Organisation and recorded in the AIP,
to the design of structures where materials used and/or the actions applied are outside the scope of
Eurocodes.
2.4
Where Eurocodes are used, information listed in Appendix A relating to the individual project, options
and choice of method adopted shall be recorded for Categories 2 and 3 structures.
2.5
Where supplementary guidance or advice that is non contradictory and complementary to Eurocodes
from recognised sources and publications from professional institutions is used, this shall be
referenced in the AIP.
2.6
Clauses in the Published Documents (PD) listed in Appendix A shall be deemed to comply with
Eurocode principles and application rules unless covered by the exceptions in clauses 2.7, 2.8 and 2.9.
NOTE
The PD clauses listed in Appendix A provide a default means of compliance with Eurocodes clauses
including situations which the Eurocode provisions are not considered to fully cover.
2.6.1
Alternative methods of complying with Eurocode clauses may be permitted.
Modifications to published documents
2.7
Types of reinforcement other than those covered in BS EN 1992-1-1 [Ref 30.N] shall not be used.
NOTE
The use of clause 4.5 of PD 6687-1 [Ref 10.I], Background paper to the UK national annex to BS EN
1992-1 is not permitted.
2.8
For lightweight road structures, the restraint on the deck of a foot/cycle track bridge shall be designed
for the action of the vehicle collision forces locally but need not be designed globally provided the
required minimum headroom is achieved.
NOTE 1
The use of the first sentence of clause 2.5.2 of PD 6688-1-7 [Ref 76.I] Recommendations for the design
of structures to BS EN 1991-1-7 is not permitted.
NOTE 2
The second sentence of clause 2.5.2 of PD 6688-1-7 [Ref 76.I] requiring restraint on the deck of
foot/cycle track bridges to prevent the deck being removed from the support under the action of the
vehicle collision forces given in NA to BS EN 1991-1-7 [Ref 104.N] remains extant.
2.9
Bridge supports shall be beyond the full normalised working width class and normalised vehicle
intrusion class of the safety barrier protecting them.
NOTE
The use of clauses 2.7.2.1.c), 2.7.2.2.b), 2.7.2.2.d) and 2.7.2.3.b) of PD 6688-1-7 [Ref 76.I]are not
permitted.

2. General design requirements
Other standards with no need for a departure
2.10
Standards used in the design of a structure shall be recorded as per the requirements of CG 300 [Ref
94.N].
2.10.1
Annex D of BS EN 15050 [Ref 63.N] may be used in the design.
NOTE
This Annex relates to bridge deck continuity at supports for decks constructed using precast concrete
elements and offers a simplified approach to dealing with redistribution effects due to creep and
shrinkage at the connection.

3. Modification design requirements
3.
Modification design requirements
3.1
Eurocodes shall be used as the basis for the design of the following modification works:
1)
strengthening or upgrading works design;
2)
structural element replacement design;
3)
component replacement design in conjunction with the relevant designated standards,
harmonised standards (hEN), UK Assessment Documents or European Assessment Documents
(EAD) for the component; and
4)
other modification design.
3.2
Where strengthening or modification of the existing structure involves deriving the resistance,
serviceability performance or durability of a section that comprises both new and existing materials
acting together, a statement shall be made in the Approval in Principle (AIP) to justify the use of
Eurocodes.
3.3
The statement made in the AIP justifying the use of Eurocodes shall take into account the properties of
the existing materials and workmanship compared to those required by the relevant European
Standards upon which the relevant Eurocodes depend.
3.4
Where modification is outside the scope of Eurocodes yet the use of Eurocodes is proposed, this shall
be justified in the AIP.
3.4.1
Where it is not possible to demonstrate the adequacy of a structural element using Eurocodes,
assessment standards may be used to re-examine particular elements/load effects for which failure is
determined.
3.5
Assessment standards shall not be used for any new element design.
14
Downloaded from https://www.standardsforhighways.co.uk on 12-Nov-2025, CD 350 Version 1.0.0, published: 30-Sep-2025

4. Reporting requirements
4.
Reporting requirements
4.1
Where a design is produced contrary to the recommendations given in a Published Document (PD),
this information shall be recorded in the AIP (or AIP addendum) for Category 2 and 3 structures.
4.2
For Category 2 and 3 structures, the use of the following clauses shall be proposed in the AIP or AIP
addendum:
1)
PD 6687-1 [Ref 10.I], clause 4.21.4; and
2)
PD 6687-2 [Ref 78.I] clauses 7.6.3 (limiting stress ranges in Tables 2A and 2B), 8.2.2, 8.2.3 (use
of guidance provided in CIRIA C660 [Ref 36.I]), 9.1 and 10.1.
4.2.1
CIRIA C766 [Ref 29.I] may be used instead of CIRIA C660 [Ref 36.I] to calculate crack widths due to
early age restraint of imposed deformation.
NOTE
CIRIA C660 [Ref 36.I] has been replaced by CIRIA C766 [Ref 29.I]. PD 6687-2 [Ref 78.I] does not
reflect this change.
4.3
Where structural elements are proposed to be designed to a higher or lower consequence class than
for the whole structure, this shall be proposed in the AIP or AIP addendum.

5. Specific design requirements
5.
Specific design requirements
5.1
The required design working life shall be defined for the individual structure in accordance with the
requirements for the technical approval of highway structures and design working life category
classifications given in Table 7.1.
Table 5.1 Design working life
Design working life category 1 (temporary structures, typically 10 years design working life)
Temporary structures (1)
Design working life category 2 (replaceable structure parts, typically 50 years design working
life)

Design working life category 3 (Short term structures, typically 50 years design working life)

Buried structures
Bridge bearings(2)
(1) Structures or parts of structures that can be dismantled with a view to being reused are not to be
considered as temporary.
(2) The design working life of bridge bearings can be reduced to 50 years subject to agreement with
the Technical approval authority (TAA).
NOTE
Requirements for permanent road restraint systems such as safety barriers and parapets are in CC 400
[Ref 58.N].
5.1.1
Unless defined in other standards or project-specific requirements, the design working life of a highway
structure should be determined, taking into account:
1)
functional requirement;
2)
safety;
3)
consequence;
4)
traffic disruption;
5)
durability;
6)
sustainability;
7)
financial; and
8)
practical feasibility if it were to be replaced in the future.

Traffic loads on bridges
Traffic loads on highway structures
5.4
Highway structures that carry traffic loads shall be designed for BS EN 1991-2 [Ref 25.N] load models
(LM) LM1, LM2 and, if appropriate for pedestrians, LM4.
5.5
Highway structures that carry motorway and all-purpose trunk road traffic shall also be designed for all
the special vehicles (SV) models given in LM3 as defined in the UK NA to BS EN 1991-2 [Ref 107.N].

5. Specific design requirements
5.6
The SV models to be used in the design shall be agreed with the TAA for the individual structure.
5.6.1
Bridges carrying motorways and all-purpose trunk roads should be designed using SV80, SV100 and
SV196.
5.6.2
The recommendations given in Table 5.6.2 should be used for bridges over motorways and all-purpose
trunk roads.
Table 5.6.2 SV models to be used in the design

Heavy load route
5.7
Where a highway structure carries traffic on a route designated as a heavy load route, the structure
shall be designed for the appropriate SOV models as defined in the UK NA to BS EN 1991-2 [Ref
107.N]and/or specific individual vehicles as required.
5.8
The appropriate SOV model shall be agreed with the TAA .
Structures which are subjected to an agreement with a third party
5.9
Accommodation bridges shall be designed for BS EN 1991-2 [Ref 25.N] load models LM1 and LM2
and, if appropriate for pedestrians, LM4.
5.10
Where the provision of a structure is the subject of an agreement with a third party, then the third party
shall notify the Overseeing Organisation of the traffic loading the structure is able to carry.
5.11
The notification of the traffic loading on the structure shall be done before any agreement is concluded
between the Overseeing Organisation and the third party.
Design for seismic resistance
5.12
Structures shall be designed to resist seismic loads in accordance with BS EN 1998-2 [Ref 42.N]where
applicable.

6. Design for durability
6.
Design for durability
Structural continuity
6.1
All bridges shall be designed as continuous over intermediate supports unless special circumstances
exist as agreed with the Overseeing Organisation.
6.1.1
Continuity may be either full continuity of the whole deck structure or partial continuity of the deck slab
alone.
6.2
All bridges with a skew angle up to 30 degrees and 60 m length or less shall be designed as integral
bridge structures.
6.2.1
Bridges with a skew angle greater than 30 degrees or lengths greater than 60 m may be designed as
integral structures.
6.3
Hinges in concrete structures shall not be used.
6.4
Half joints shall not be used in structures.
NOTE
Further guidance about structural continuity can be found in CIRIA C543 [Ref 14.I].
Expansion joints
6.5
Structures with expansion joints shall include measures for water management as per CD 357 [Ref 5.N]
and CG 300 [Ref 94.N].
Post-tensioning
6.6
Precast segmental post-tensioned concrete structures with an internal grouted system shall not be
used.
6.6.1
Precast segmental structures incorporating continuous external post-tensioned duct systems, and
precast non-segmental construction with either external or internal continuous duct systems, may be
designed providing that post-tensioned structures using external systems or unbonded tendons are
detailed such that inspection of all individual tendons and their eventual replacement is possible without
restricting traffic.
External prestressing
6.7
All external and unbonded tendons shall be replaceable without having to restrict traffic on the highway.
6.8
Provision shall be made for the inspection and maintenance of external tendons.
Access
6.9
Access shall be provided for the following purposes:
1)
all maintenance activities, including cleaning and painting, routine maintenance, jacking, removal
or replacement of bearings; and
2)
inspection of closed cell and box members.
6.9.1
Access should be provided from below deck level to avoid access from the upper surfaces of bridge
decks.
6.9.2
Galleries should be provided below abutment deck joints.
6.9.3
Galleries should be provided with at least two points of access/egress.
6.10
Access facilities provided for inspection and maintenance shall be secure, preventing access by
unauthorised personal.
6.11
Access openings shall be watertight.
20
Downloaded from https://www.standardsforhighways.co.uk on 12-Nov-2025, CD 350 Version 1.0.0, published: 30-Sep-2025

6. Design for durability
6.12
Water and debris shall not be permitted to accumulate on or around openings.
6.13
Ventilation shall be provided to all accessible closed cell or box sections.
6.13.1
Ventilation provisions should be detailed to prevent them acting as a conduit for water ingress.
6.14
Water shall not accumulate in closed cell and box sections.
6.14.1
Where provided, drainage holes should permit inspection access using endoscopic type equipment.
6.14.2
In closed sections where access for inspection is provided, provision for artificial lighting should be
made.
NOTE 1
Access points can be at each end of the structure at points that are safe and easily accessible and do
not require traffic control. Means of access can include gantries, walkways, scaffolding ladders, rails or
aerial work platform.
NOTE 2
Additional information on access for maintenance and repair is given in CIRIA C686 [Ref 20.I].
Water management
6.15
Surface water shall be removed from decks through appropriate water management plans.
6.15.1
Drainage systems in structures should:
1)
include sub-surface drains;
2)
minimise blockage and the requirement for cleaning;
3)
minimise traffic management during cleaning operations;
4)
be sufficiently robust to withstand damage during cleaning;
5)
be resistant to all commonly occurring chemical spillage;
6)
include facilities for rodding and other necessary maintenance for closed systems;
7)
restrict surface water from falling freely from bridge decks;
8)
include drainage provision for service bays;
9)
include drainage provision for voids; and
10)
include sealed access hatches or manhole covers for box members to prevent leakage into the
box.
6.16
Drainage details integral with the structure shall not be used.
6.17
Downpipes cast into piers shall not be used.
6.18
Drainage water from bridge decks shall not be discharged into the drainage layers in the vicinity of
piers and behind abutments.
6.18.1
All gullies should be fully trapped.
6.18.2
Water from the approaches to structures should be prevented from entering the structure.
NOTE
By far the most serious source of damage is salty water leaking through joints in the deck or service
ducts, and poor, faulty or badly maintained drainage systems. Of crucial importance is the provision of
a positive, well designed, detailed and constructed drainage system for managing water from the deck
and into a drainage system.
6.19
Ventilation and drainage holes shall be provided to reduce condensation and eliminate any ponding
inside the box as a result of a possible ingress of water.
6.19.1
Ventilation and drainage holes should be detailed to prevent access and colonisation by birds and
animals.
21

6. Design for durability
Groundwater management
6.20
A positive drainage system consisting of a permeable vertical drainage layer and a system of pipes to
collect and remove water shall be provided within backfill materials or other retained ground behind
earth retaining structures to control groundwater levels.
6.20.1
A permeable drainage layer behind gravity and semi-gravity walls should be provided where backfill
materials are classified either as cohesionless soils with medium to low permeability (2 x 10-5 m/s or
less) or as cohesive soils.
NOTE 1
A permeable vertical drainage layer behind earth retaining structures is important to limit horizontal
water pressure on the wall as without effective drainage, water pressure can rise and exceed values
assumed by the design.
NOTE 2
Further guidance on types of drainage layers can be found in BS 8002 [Ref 23.I].
6.20.2
Vertical drainage layers behind earth retaining structures should be designed to allow for the following:
1)
changes in groundwater levels (temporary or permanent) due to construction of the earth
retaining structure;
2)
the quantities, pressures and eventual chemical content of any water expected to discharge from
the positive drainage system; and
3)
preventing fine-grained material in the backfill from entering and clogging the drainage layer and
reducing its permeability.
6.20.3
Vertical drainage layers should extend over the full length of the earth retaining structure and the full
height of structure above collecting pipes/carrier drains.
6.20.4
Vertical drainage layers behind gravity and semi-gravity earth retaining structures should consist of a
permitted permeable backing material type given in Appendix G of this document.
6.21
Groundwater diverted by the vertical drainage layer behind gravity and semi-gravity retaining walls
shall be collected in porous or perforated carrier pipes located at the bottom of the drainage layer.
6.21.1
The permeable vertical drainage layer for gravity or semi-gravity walls may be supplemented with weep
pipes provided through the wall thickness but not at locations where the water can discharge onto
areas used by the public.
NOTE 1
Collecting pipes and carrier drains can eventually fill and block with silt, allowing groundwater levels to
rise again. Weep pipes are provided as backup to the main positive drainage system in the event of
blockage to relieve the build-up of water pressure.
NOTE 2
Water issuing from weep pipes can be a potential indicator of malfunction in the primary drainage
system.
NOTE 3
Fine material in the backfill can be washed out through weep pipes unless the pipes are provided with a
backfall towards the fill.
6.21.2
Where weep pipes are provided through the wall, hard paved areas in front of the wall should be sloped
towards the carriageway with at least a standard crossfall in accordance with CG 501 [Ref 17.N].
NOTE
Water issuing through weep pipes and allowed to pond on paved areas can freeze when the ambient
temperature is low.
6.21.3
Water collected in the permeable vertical drainage layer should be carried away from the highway
structure in pipes and discharged in a manner that is safe and compliant with environmental regulations
in accordance with CG 501 [Ref 17.N]and LA 113 [Ref 72.N].
6.22
Features for controlling the build up of water pressure behind non-gravity types of retaining walls shall
be provided.
6.22.1
Weepholes should be provided through all impermeable non-gravity types of retaining wall or facing
and though walls of concrete boxes if there is no alternative positive drainage system.
22
Downloaded from https://www.standardsforhighways.co.uk on 12-Nov-2025, CD 350 Version 1.0.0, published: 30-Sep-2025



======================================================================
PAGE 24 of 417
======================================================================
CD 350 Version 1.0.0
6. Design for durability
NOTE
Non-gravity retaining walls include embedded retaining walls (see BS 8002 [Ref 23.I]). Cofferdams,
basements and strutted excavations are intended to exclude water so do not need weep pipes unless
required by the design.
6.22.2
Where highway structures are constructed off-line and subsequently jacked into position in close
contact with the ground, elements retaining the ground should be provided with a permeable vertical
drainage layer.
6.23
Where safety and serviceability of a retaining structure depends on a positive drainage system
continuing to be effective, design of the positive drainage system shall include one or more of the
following features:
1)
declaration of the maintenance regime and required frequency for the positive drainage system in
accordance with CG 302 [Ref 3.N];
2)
sufficient hydraulic capacity to ensure the positive drainage system performs adequately for the
structure design life without maintenance; or
3)
a positive drainage system consisting of primary and secondary ("backup") parts to prevent
leakage from the primary system from entering the ground beneath or next to the structure.
NOTE
A secondary (backup) drainage system can comprise a separate pipe enclosing the primary drainage
system or a channel below the primary drainage system.
Waterproofing
6.24
The deck shall be provided with a waterproofing system according to CD 358 [Ref 109.N].
6.25
Abutment galleries and service bays shall have all exposed concrete surfaces waterproofed.
6.26
The following concrete surfaces shall be waterproofed:
1)
vertical faces at deck ends and abutment curtain walls;
2)
top faces of piers and abutment bearing shelves;
3)
inaccessible areas which can be subject to leakage, for instance beam ends; and
4)
buried concrete surfaces.
NOTE
The most important properties of an effective waterproofing system are its waterproofing ability and its
bond to the deck. If bonding is effective over the whole deck area, then any local lack of watertightness
in the waterproofing layer is incapable of causing significant damage to the deck.
Cladding
6.27
Where external cladding is used, the fixings for the cladding shall use corrosion resistant materials.
6.27.1
Detailing of cladding systems should allow easy removal for the purpose of principal inspection of the
structure, or for maintenance work.

Note A1. Traffic restrictions may not be appropriate for highly utilised structures with high delay costs.
Note A2. Either the 'safe life' method ( PD 6695-1-9 [Ref 80.I] clause 5.2) or 'damage tolerant' method (
PD 6695-1-9 [Ref 80.I] clause 5.3) should be used.
Note A3. The gross geometrical stress concentrating effects listed are not exhaustive and designers
should consider other cases as appropriate.
Note A4. The clauses are not covered by Eurocodes.
Note A5. Should be used if second order analysis is not undertaken.
Note A6. If computer analysis is used designers should take these stresses into account.
Note A7. Other load effects including but not limited to differential settlement, soil pressures and wind
may need to be considered.
Note A8. The specific requirements for the design of plated diaphragms, cross frames, the design for
torsion and distortion, are not given in Eurocodes. However the reference clauses should provide the
necessary guidance.
Note A9. Should be used where simple calculation methods without use of computer software are to be
used.

CD 350 Version 1.0.0
Appendix B. Project specific information to be recorded
Appendix B. Project specific information to be recorded
B1
Notes on the specific information to be recorded
The information is categorised as "Core" or "Special". "Core" indicates that information should be
recorded in all cases. "Special" indicates that information is only to be recorded in special cases where
it is applicable to the project.
The location for the information to be recorded may be the relevant part of the AIP, or if the information
does not require technical approval then it may be recorded in the Designer Record.
The Designer Record may need to be passed to the checker or the contractor but is not submitted to
the TAA.
Specific cases for which information or assumptions should be communicated to the contractor are
highlighted in the "Category" column with a reference to note [1].
It is the responsibility of the compiler of the AIP and Designer Record to ensure that the Standards,
references and clauses listed are relevant and up-to date.
Where the information to be recorded in the AIP is not available at the time of its submission, this
should be noted. The information should be added to the AIP or AIP addendum when available.
B1.1
Additional Notes referenced in tables below:
[1]. The Designer should ensure that information or assumptions that affect the execution are
communicated to the contractor, for example, by including relevant information on the drawings.
[2]. The Designer Record should be used to record decisions that affect the design of the permanent
works. For the technical approval of temporary works, it is typically appropriate to record this
information in the AIP instead of the Designer Record.
B2
Tables to record specific information
The following tables set out the information that should be recorded for each project.
43

For highway structures built in

Class 3, an independent third
party inspection of the
execution is required when the
structure or parts of it are
designated as Inspection Level
3 to BS EN 1990 [Ref 43.N]in
accordance with Section 5.
Reason for independent third
party inspection of the
execution
Provide the reason for the need
of an independent third party
inspection of the execution of
structural concrete works for
the structural element and/or its
part.
Inspection Level 3 to BS EN
1990 [Ref 43.N]requires an
independent third party
inspection of the execution for
parts or whole of structures.
Inspection Level 3, and the
consequent need for an
independent third party
inspection of the execution,
should be specified for parts or
whole of Category 3 structures
to CG 300 [Ref 94.N]for which
the execution is complex or the
quality of the execution is
critical for the structural stability
and/or future maintenance,
such as parts difficult to inspect
in service.

inspection of the execution

documentation containing the
detailed specification
requirements for the
independent third party
inspection of the execution of

element and/or its part.

allocated to every document
where detailed specification
requirements for the
independent third party
inspection of the execution are
given for the structural element
and/or its part. The
documentation shall clearly
detail the scope and extent of
the independent third party
inspection and any specific
reporting requirements.

Non-destructive testing required
Indicate whether
non-destructive testing is
required for the structural
element and/or its part.
Permitted option limited to: yes,
no.
Non-destructive testing for a
structural element and/or its
part is required routinely only in
specific situations already
covered by specification
requirements, such as
non-destructive testing
performed to check the
concrete cover to
reinforcement. However, it may
be invoked in special cases, for
example where inspection for
execution or results of identity
testing has led to doubt
regarding the works. Advice on
non-destructive testing is given
in Appendix I.

non-destructive testing
including frequency (where
applicable)
Provide the requirements for
non-destructive testing for the
structural element and/or its
part, such as the type, extent
and frequency of
non-destructive testing.
Only applies when
non-destructive testing is
required. Design requirements
and advice for the provision of
requirements for
non-destructive testing are
given in Appendix I.
Destructive testing required
Indicate whether destructive
testing is required for the
structural element and/or its
part. Permitted option limited to:
yes, no.
Destructive testing, such as
testing of cores taken from the
structural element and/or its
part, is not routinely required
but it may be invoked in special
cases, for example where
inspection for execution or
results of other tests, such as
identity testing and/or
subsequent non-destructive
testing, has led to doubt
regarding the works. Advice on
destructive testing is given in
Appendix I.
Requirements for destructive
testing including frequency
(where applicable)
Provide the requirements for
destructive testing for the
structural element and/or its
part, such as the type, extent
and frequency of destructive
testing.
Only applies when destructive
testing is required. Design
requirements and advice for the
provision of requirements for
destructive testing are given in
Appendix I.

Appendix C. Design outputs for structural concrete
Table C.5 Design outputs for special testing requirements for the inspection of execution for
structural concrete (continued)
Dimensional accuracy testing
required
Indicate whether dimensional
accuracy testing is required for
the structural element and/or its
part. Permitted option limited to:
yes, no.
For both in situ and precast
structural concrete elements,
there may be circumstances
where the dimensional
accuracy of both the finished
product and their positioning in
the works, within the tolerances
specified, is of particular
importance for their execution
and/or function in service or
where inspection for execution
or results of other tests has led
to doubt regarding the works. In
such cases, dimensional
accuracy testing, in the form of
specific requirements for
measurement of the
dimensional accuracy of
structural elements and/or their
parts over and above the
routine quality control, may
need to be specified. Examples
include where the effect of
temperature, shrinkage or
imposed load/deformation on
the geometry are significant;
where methods of construction
are used for which the
dimensional accuracy and
positioning is critical, such as
balanced cantilever; where the
positions of bars, tendons or
ducts within the concrete
section is specified to be within
a project-specific tolerance;
where twist, bow, squareness,
flatness, camber and/or upward
deflection of precast concrete
elements is critical to their
positioning in the works. Advice
on dimensional accuracy
testing is given in Appendix I.
Requirements for dimensional
accuracy testing including
frequency (where applicable)
Provide the requirements for
dimensional accuracy testing
for the structural element and/or
its part, such as the type, extent
and frequency of dimensional
accuracy testing.
Only applies when dimensional
accuracy testing is required.
Design requirements and
advice for the provision of
requirements for dimensional
accuracy testing are given in
Appendix I.

Load testing required

required for the structure and/or
the structural element and/or its
part. Permitted option limited to:
yes, no.
Load testing of a structural
element and/or its part or the
entire structure is not routinely
required but it may be invoked
in special cases, for example
where inspection for execution
or results of other tests, such as
identity testing and/or
subsequent non-destructive
testing, destructive testing or
dimensional accuracy testing,
has led to doubt regarding the
works. In such cases, load
testing on individual structural
elements, either in-situ or
precast, or on the entire
structure may be specified.
Advice on load testing is given
in Appendix I.

including frequency (where

load testing, such as the type,

specific structural element
and/or its part) and frequency of

is required. Design
requirements and advice for the
provision of requirements for
load testing are given in

documentation reference(s)
Provide reference(s) of the
documentation containing the

requirements for any special
testing required.
Is/are the unique reference(s)
allocated to every document
where the detailed specification
requirements for any special
testing specified are given for
the structural element and/or its
part. The documentation shall
clearly detail the scope, type,
extent, frequency, methods and
acceptance criteria of special
testing and any specific
reporting requirements. Further
design requirements and advice
for the provision of special
testing specification
requirements are given in
Appendix I.

Design output / Reference

Structure ID
Provide the unique identifying
reference of the structure.
Is the unique reference
allocated to each structure
within a scheme.
Permanent soffit formwork
reference
Provide the permanent soffit
formwork reference.
Is the unique reference
allocated to the permanent soffit
formwork itself.
Type of permanent soffit
formwork
Provide the type of permanent
soffit formwork, such as precast
reinforced concrete plank (floor
plates); profiled steel sheeting
(PSS); glassfibre reinforced
concrete (GRC); glass
reinforced polymer (GRP); or
other.
Design requirements and
advice for permanent soffit
formwork are given in CD 359
[Ref 21.N]. Participating
formwork can be achieved with
precast reinforced concrete
plank (floor plates), whilst
profiled steel sheeting (PSS),
glassfibre reinforced concrete
(GRC) and glass reinforced
polmer (GRP) are assumed as
non-participating.
The design outputs shall
require that GRC permanent
soffit formwork is only specified
as flat single skin panels or
corrugated single skin panels
with no polystyrene formers in
the corrugations.
The design outputs shall
require that PSS permanent
soffit formwork is only specified
with no indentations, because
indentations in PSS can form a
shear connection with the
in-situ concrete and lead to
fatigue-induced cracking in
service.
Structural element supporting
permanent soffit formwork
reference(s)
Provide the reference of the
structural element(s) supporting
the permanent soffit formwork.
Is the unique reference
allocated to each structural
element within a structure on
which the permanent soffit
formwork is supported (e.g. a
steel or concrete beam).
Description of structural
element(s) supporting
permanent soffit formwork
Provide a description of the
structural element(s) and/or
its/their part(s) supporting the
permanent soffit formwork.
This/these may be the entire
structural element(s) or a part of
it/them.

Provide the required method of
determination of the essential
characteristics when the

concrete plank (floor plates)
type. Permitted option limited

reinforced concrete plank (floor

concrete plank (floor plates)

performance requirements
specified directly as a design
output, with no detailed design
documentation provided.

where the permanent soffit

on the basis of a 'design
specification' via provision of
detailed design documentation
and drawings/models.

Table C.7 Design outputs for the frequency of suitability testing of permanent soffit formwork

Design output / Reference
Information to be provided as
design outputs
Design requirements, advice

The frequency of suitability
testing of permanent soffit
formwork other than precast
reinforced concrete plank (floor
plates)
Provide the required frequency
of suitability testing of
permanent soffit formwork other
than precast reinforced
concrete plank (floor plates), if
different from the default.
Suitability testing is required for
permanent soffit formwork other
than precast reinforced
concrete plank (floor plates).
Data from previous tests
provided by the supplier can
fulfil this purpose without the
need for suitability testing to be
performed at the construction
stage, but such data may not
always be available, for
example if the type or layout of
the permanent soffit formwork is
unusual.
The default required frequency
of suitability testing is three
tests for each different type,
manufacturing process, product
composition, layout, span
length and cross section of
permanent soffit formwork unit
proposed for use in the works.
The frequency may be
increased when the specified
permanent soffit formwork is
subject to unusual load
conditions or has specific load
testing requirements specified.

and with any soffit formwork, shall
be specified at each end of the
void former and at any low point
along the void length to prevent
accumulation of water inside the
void.

Appendix C. Design outputs for structural concrete
Table C.13 Design outputs for the frequency of determination of the compressive strength of
concrete in the new parts of the deck in the formation of continuity joints in bridge decks before
the formwork can be removed
Design output / Reference
Information to be provided as
design outputs
Design requirements, advice
or notes for design outputs
The frequency of determination
of the compressive strength of
the concrete in the new parts of
the deck in the formation of
continuity joints in bridge decks
with the purpose of justifying the
timeline of formwork removal
Provide the required frequency
of compressive strength testing
of the concrete in the new parts
of the deck in the formation of
continuity joints in bridge decks
before the formwork can be
removed, if different from the
default.
The default is testing
specimens at 7 days after
concrete placing and thereafter
every 24 hours until the
compressive strength reaches
the value corresponding to the
compressive strength class
specified for the new parts of
the deck, with the compressive
strength evaluated from two
test specimens made from one
sample for each age of testing
taken randomly from an amount
of concrete representing no
more than the lesser of 4
batches or 24 m3, but with no
less than one sample per day of
concreting.
This acknowledges the fact
that, also given that early
removal of formwork leads to a
higher initial deflection in the
new part of the deck prior to the
concrete maturing, the
formwork in the new part of the
deck should not be removed
until the compressive strength
class specified for the new parts
of the deck is reached, and in
any case no earlier than 7 days
after concrete placing to cater
for the strength development of
different concrete mixes - but it
gives the flexibility to be able to
provide a more or less stringent
testing regime and timeline, for
example to suit the timeline of
specific construction stages for
the works; traffic management
restrictions; hot/cold weather
working; the use of concrete
with rapid/slow setting time; the
overall project specific
formwork removal requirements
for the structural element and/or
its part.
Further advice is provided in
CD 364 [Ref 48.N].
121

design outputs

or notes for design outputs

Provide the unique identifying
reference of the structure.
Is the unique reference
allocated to each structure
within a scheme.
Structural element reference
Provide the structural element
reference.
Is the unique reference
allocated to each structural
element within a structure
supported by
falsework/formwork.
Description of structural
element
Provide a description of the
structural element and/or its
part supported by
falsework/formwork, including
whether concrete is supported
in bending or in compression.
This may be the entire
structural element or a part of it.
Elements in bending (decks,
beams and slabs) and elements
in compression (columns, piers
and abutments) rely on different
values to be reached for the
strength of the concrete before
the formwork can be removed
safely.
Drawing/model reference(s)
Provide reference of drawing(s)
or model(s) where the structural
element and/or its part
supported by

and/or its part supported by

details of any required
deflection profile to be achieved
after removal of the
falsework/formwork, which may
influence the degree of restraint
that falsework/formwork can
impose on the element and/or
its part and the removal
sequence. Drawing(s)/model(s)
shall also show details of any
backpropping/re-propping.

Downloaded from https://www.standardsforhighways.co.uk on 12-Nov-2025, CD 350 Version 1.0.0, published: 30-Sep-2025

Appendix C. Design outputs for structural concrete
Table C.14 Design outputs for requirements for removal of falsework and formwork for
structural concrete (continued)
Minimum concrete compressive
cube strength before removal of
formwork
Provide the minimum
compressive cube strength
required for the concrete in the
structural element and/or its
part before removal of formwork
is permitted. Provide value in
MPa.
Formwork supporting concrete
in bending shall not be removed
until the concrete compressive
cube strength has reached 15
MPa, or the value required by
the design, whichever is
greater; formwork supporting
concrete in compression shall
not be removed until the
concrete compressive cube
strength has reached 3 MPa, or
the value required by the
design, whichever is greater.
The limit for concrete in bending
is to ensure enough strength for
the element to support its self
weight for all or part of the
structural span has been
gained, whilst the limit for
concrete in compression is to
ensure concrete is strong
enough to resist the adhesion at
the interface with the formwork.
A lower minimum compressive
cube strength value may be
provided with justification from
calculations based on the
properties of the proposed
concrete mix, as long as any
impact on the deflection profile
and crack control is also taken
into account.
Notwithstanding the above, for
formwork in new parts of the
deck in the formation of
continuity joints in bridge decks,
the minimum compressive cube
strength before removal of
forrmwork in the new parts of
the deck is permitted shall not
be less than that corresponding
to the specified compressive
strength class of the concrete
for the new parts of the deck.

Appendix C. Design outputs for structural concrete
Table C.14 Design outputs for requirements for removal of falsework and formwork for
structural concrete (continued)
Backpropping and/or
re-propping required
Provide whether backpropping
and/or re-propping following
formwork removal is required
for the structural element and/or
its part. Permitted option limited
to: yes, no.
Backpropping is when
falsework in the form of props is
needed through several levels
of a structure, for example to
allow temporary loads to be
carried without overloading any
one level. Re-propping is when
formwork is struck from the
structural element and/or its
part, for example to speed up
its removal and allow re-use
elsewhere, and the structural
element and/or its part is then
propped, with the sequence
repeated until all formwork is
removed and the soffit is fully
propped. Whilst they are more
common in a building structures
context, they may be used in a
highway structures context if
catered for in design. Additional
guidance is provided in CS 030
[Ref 44.I].
Backpropping and/or
re-propping duration following
formwork removal (where
applicable)
Provide the duration for
backpropping and/or
re-propping to be kept in place
after formwork is removed for
the structural element and/or its
part. Provide value in days.
Only applies when
backpropping and/or
re-propping is specified for a
structural element and/or its
part. The duration for it to be
kept in place will depend on any
specific sequencing of removal
and should be selected upon
justification based on
calculations taking into account
the concrete strengths,
deflection profile and crack
control. Additional guidance is
provided in CS 030 [Ref 44.I].
Where a frequency of determination of the compressive strength of concrete before the formwork can
be removed that is different from the default frequency in Table C.15 is required, the design outputs
shall be provided in accordance with Table C.15.
Table C.15 Design outputs for the frequency of determination of the compressive strength of
concrete before the formwork can be removed
Design output / Reference
Information to be provided as
design outputs
Design requirements, advice
or notes for design outputs

CD 350 Version 1.0.0
Appendix C. Design outputs for structural concrete
The frequency of determination
of the compressive strength of
concrete before the formwork
can be removed
Provide the required frequency
of compressive strength testing
of concrete before the formwork
can be removed, if different
from the default.
The default is testing specimens
every 24 hours after concrete
placing until the compressive
strength reaches the minimum
value specified as safe for the
formwork removal, with the
compressive strength evaluated
from four test specimens made
from one sample for each age
of testing, taken randomly from
an amount of concrete
representing no more than the
lesser of 4 batches or 24 m3,
but with no less than one
sample per day of concreting.
This acknowledges the fact that
the formwork should not be
removed until the minimum
specified compressive strength
is reached - but it gives the
flexibility to be able to provide a
more or less stringent testing
regime and timeline, for
example to suit the timeline of
specific construction stages for
the works; traffic management
restrictions; hot/cold weather
working; the use of concrete
with rapid/slow setting time; the
overall project specific
formwork removal requirements
for the structural element and/or
its part.
For formwork in new parts of
the deck in the formation of
continuity joints in bridge decks,
the default is testing specimens
at 7 days after concrete placing
and thereafter every 24 hours
until the compressive strength
reaches the value
corresponding to the
compressive strength class
specified for the new parts of
the deck; this is because
ensuring that the concrete
strength prior to the removal of
forrmwork in the new parts of
the deck in the formation of
continuity joints in bridge decks
is no less than that
corresponding to the specified
compressive strength class of
the concrete for the new parts
of the deck, mitigates against
unintended differential
deflections and/or cracking at
the longitudinal deck interfaces
upon formwork removal.
127

Appendix C. Design outputs for structural concrete
Table C.16 Design outputs for hot rolled and cold worked carbon steel bars for the
reinforcement of structural concrete (continued)
Notation of steel reinforcement
for hot rolled and cold worked
carbon steel bars
Provide the notation of steel
reinforcement to BS 8666 [Ref
73.N]for hot rolled and cold
worked carbon steel bars in the
structural element and/or its
part. Permitted option limited to:
B, C.
BS 4449 [Ref 87.N]specifies
three standard grades (B500A,
B500B and B500C). With the
exception of grade B500A for
nominal sizes below 8 mm,
these grades conform to the
requirements of BS EN
1992-1-1 [Ref 30.N]. Grades B5
00B and B500C conform to the
requirements of BS EN 1992-2
[Ref 28.N], where the use of
ductility class A reinforcement
is not permitted; the NA to BS
EN 1992 [Ref 106.N] permits
the use of ductility class A only
for fabric reinforcement,
provided it is not taken into
account in the evaluation of the
ultimate resistance.
Therefore, for hot rolled and
cold worked carbon steel bars
the use of grade B500A is not
permitted.
Ductility class B is the default
choice; however, ductility class
C may be specified in cases
where higher ductility is
required, for example when the
design relies on moment
redistribution, there are specific
requirements for robustness or
there are requirements for
resistance to specific cyclic
loading such as seismic
loading.
Reinforcement bending
schedule reference(s)
Provide reference(s) of the
reinforcement bending
schedule for hot rolled and cold
worked carbon steel bars in the
structural element and/or its
part.
Is/are the unique reference(s)
allocated to every reinforcement
bending schedule within a
scheme related to the structural
element and/or its part
containing hot rolled and cold
worked carbon steel bars.

Notation of steel
reinforcement for steel
fabric
Provide the notation of steel
reinforcement to BS 8666 [Ref
73.N] for steel fabric in the
structural element and/or its part.

standard grades (B500A, B500B
and B500C). With the exception of
grade B500A for nominal sizes
below 8 mm, these grades conform
to the requirements of BS EN
1992-1-1 [Ref 30.N]. Grades B500B
and B500C conform to the

class A reinforcement is not
permitted; however, the NA to BS
EN 1992 [Ref 106.N] permits the
use of ductility class A for fabric
reinforcement provided it is not
taken into account in the evaluation
of the ultimate resistance.

reinforcing steel is permitted for a
nominal size equal to or above 6
mm, whilst the use of grade B500A
reinforcing steel is only permitted
for a nominal size equal to or above
8 mm when not designing for ULS
(Ultimate Limit State).
Reinforcement used in the
production of steel fabrics subject to
fatigue loading is specified to the
grades of BS 4449 [Ref 87.N],
because standardised grades of
reinforcement subject to fatigue
loading are not defined in BS 4483
[Ref 86.N].
For ULS design, ductility class B is
the default choice; however,
ductility class C may be specified in
cases where higher ductility is
required, for example when the
design relies on moment
redistribution, there are specific
requirements for robustness or
there are requirements for
resistance to specific cyclic loading
such as seismic loading.

structural element and/or its part
incorporating dowels is shown.
Is/are the unique reference(s)
allocated to every drawing/model
within a scheme showing the
structural element and/or its part
containing dowels where
detailing, dimensions,
designation and location of the
dowels within the concrete are
indicated. Only plain round bars
made of stainless steel are
permitted as dowels for use in
structural concrete.
Steel designation number for
stainless steel dowels
Provide the steel designation
number to BS EN 10088-1 [Ref
84.N] for stainless steel dowels in
the structural element and/or its
part.
Since there are multiple chemical
grades of stainless steel, the
required stainless steel dowels
shall be correctly specified and
clearly designated. The selection
of the required stainless steel
designation number should be
based on the guidance provided
in Annex A of BS EN 1993-1-4
[Ref 36.N]and Annex B of BS
6744 [Ref 87.I].
0.2% proof strength (yield
strength) of stainless steel
dowels
Provide the 0.2% proof strength
(MPa) required to BS EN
10088-5 [Ref 85.N] for the
stainless steel dowels in the
structural element and/or its part.
The 0.2% proof strength shall be
selected from design
considerations, ensuring that the
specified strength is compatible
with the steel designation
number specified.

CD 350 Version 1.0.0
Appendix C. Design outputs for structural concrete
Table C.21 Design outputs for steel reinforcement couplers for use in structural concrete
(continued)
Drawing or model reference(s)
Provide reference of the
relevant drawing(s)/model(s)
where the structural element
and/or its part containing steel
reinforcement couplers is
shown.
Is/are the unique reference(s)
allocated to every drawing/model
within a scheme showing the
structural element and/or its part
containing steel reinforcement
couplers, where detailing and
location of the couplers within the
concrete, and the designation for
stainless steel couplers, are
indicated.
Type of steel reinforcement
coupler
Provide the type of coupler to
be used in the structural
element and/or its part.
A number of systems are
available for jointing reinforcing
bars which are capable of
transmitting the tensile and
compressive forces in the bar;
these include, but are not limited
to, the following:
1) swaged couplers
2) tapered threaded bars and
couplers
3) upset bar ends with parallel
threads and couplers
4) couplers fixed to the bars with
studs for transmitting
compressive forces only
5) sleeves with tapered closers
that align the square sawn
ends of bars for transmitting
compressive forces only.
Grouted couplers are not
permitted for use, due to concerns
regarding quality control of
installation and their ability to
meet fatigue requirements.
Steel reinforcement coupler
material type
Provide the material type for
the steel reinforcement coupler
to be used in the structural
element and/or its part.
Permitted option limited to:
carbon steel, stainless steel.
Steel reinforcement couplers shall
have durability equivalent to or
better than that of the steel
reinforcement being coupled in
the structural element and/or its
part. Hence, when stainless steel
reinforcement is being coupled,
the coupler should be of stainless
steel.

Appendix C. Design outputs for structural concrete
Table C.22 Design outputs for the characteristics of the structural element and/or its part where
post-installed reinforcing bar connections are to be installed (continued)
Compressive strength class of
the concrete base material
Provide the compressive
strength class of the concrete
base material for the structural
element and/or its part where
the post-installed reinforcing bar
connections are to be installed.
This is one of the classes in
Tables 12 and 13 of BS EN 206
[Ref 11.N]and Table A.3 of BS
8500-2 [Ref 13.N]and is the
concrete compressive strength
class of the new or existing
element receiving the
post-installed reinforcing bar
connections. As the relevant
UKADs/EADs may only cater
for either a C20/25 or a C50/60
compressive strength as
representative of a 'low' or 'high'
strength of the base material, in
the subsequent selection of the
product the closest value to the
actual concrete compressive
class specified will be used.
Applicable exposure class
Provide the applicable exposure
class to BS 8500-1 [Ref 12.N]
for the structural element and/or
its part where the post-installed
reinforcing bar connections are
to be installed.
Design requirements and
advice on the selection of the
applicable exposure classes for
a structural element and/or its
part are given in Appendix I.
Chloride content class of the
concrete base material
Provide the chloride content
class of the concrete base
material of the structural
element and/or its part where
the post-installed reinforcing bar
connections are to be installed.
In accordance with Table C.36,
the permitted chloride content
classes for highway structures
are Cl 0,10, Cl 0,20, Cl 0,30 and
Cl 1,00, with further guidance
provided in BS 8500-1 [Ref
12.N]and BS 8500-2 [Ref 13.N].
As the relevant UKADs/EADs
may only cater for either a 0,20
or a 0,40 chloride content class
as representative of a 'low' or
'high' chloride content in the
base material, in the
subsequent selection of the
product the closest value to the
actual concrete chloride content
class specified will be used.

Appendix C. Design outputs for structural concrete
Table C.22 Design outputs for the characteristics of the structural element and/or its part where
post-installed reinforcing bar connections are to be installed (continued)
Limit/constraint to the force(s)
to be applied by the reinforcing
bar connection(s) to avoid
damage to, or instability of, the
structural element and/or its
part
Provide any limit/constraint to
the force(s) to be applied onto
the structural element via the
post-installed reinforcing bar
connection(s) to avoid damage
to the structural element and/or
its part.
There may be situations where
the arrangement and/or
ultimate load capacity of the
post-installed reinforcing bar
connection(s) lead to force(s)
applied to the structural element
and/or its part which are higher
than the force(s) the structural
element and/or its part can
withstand without suffering
damage or instability. Providing
a limit/constraint to the force(s)
to be applied ensures that only
post-installed reinforcing bar
connections transmitting
maximum forces below such
limits/constraints are used.
Limit/constraint to the concrete
base material hole(s)
diameter/length
Provide any limit/constraint to
the diameter/length of the
hole(s) in the concrete base
material of the structural
element and/or its part where
the post-installed reinforcing bar
connections are to be installed.
There may be situations where
the diameter and/or length of
the hole(s) in the concrete base
material are restricted due to
the specific layout of the
structural element and/or its
part receiving the post-installed
reinforcing bar connection.
Providing a limit/constraint
ensures that only post-installed
reinforcing bar connections of
diameter and length within such
limit/constraint are used.
Direction of installation of the
post-installed reinforcing bar
connections into the structural
element and/or its part in
accordance with the
UKAD/EAD
Provide the requirement, in
accordance with the relevant
UKAD/EAD, for the
post-installed reinforcing bar
connections to be installed into
the structural element and/or its
part at specific directions.
Permitted multiple option limited
to: D1, D2, D3, vertically
downward, horizontal, vertically
upwards.
Design requirements, advice
and definitions on the permitted
options for the direction of
installation of post-installed
reinforcing bar connections are
given in CD 372 [Ref 20.N],
also with reference to the UK
designated pre-Exit EAD (that
permits vertically downward,
horizontal and vertically
upwards) and the current EAD
(that permits D1, D2 and D3).
As post-installed reinforcing bar
connections complying with
either the UK designated
pre-Exit or the current EAD may
be used, the selected options
should cover both scenarios.
Where post-installed reinforcing bar connections are required, the design outputs for systems for
post-installed reinforcing bar connections shall be provided in accordance with Table C.23.
Table C.23 Design outputs for systems for post-installed reinforcing bar connections

safety critical, non-safety

advice on the safety criticality of
post-installed reinforcing bar
connections are given in CD

Design working life of the
post-installed reinforcing bar
connections
Provide the design working life
of the post-installed reinforcing
bar connections to be installed
into the structural element
and/or its part. Provide value in
years.
Design requirements and
advice on the required design
working life of post-installed
reinforcing bar connections are
given in CD 372 [Ref 20.N], with
reference to Section 5. The
UKADs/EADs cater for a 50 or
100 years design working life.
Type of reinforcing bar in the
post-installed reinforcing bar
connections
Provide the type of reinforcing
bar to be used in the
post-installed reinforcing bar
connections to be installed into
the structural element and/or its
part. Permitted option limited to:
carbon steel grade B500B to
BS 4449 [Ref 87.N], carbon
steel grade B500C to BS 4449
[Ref 87.N], stainless steel grade
B500B to BS 6744 [Ref 87.I].
For carbon steel, ductility class
B is the default choice;
however, ductility class C may
be specified in cases where
higher ductility is required, for
example when the design relies
on moment redistribution, there
are specific requirements for
robustness or there are
requirements for resistance to
specific cyclic loading such as
seismic loading. Design
requirements and advice on the
specification of stainless steel
reinforcing bar connections are
given in CD 372 [Ref 20.N], with
further advice on the reason for
using stainless steel bars given
in Appendix I.
Corrosion resistance class to
Annex A of BS EN 1993-1-4 for
the stainless steel of the
post-installed reinforcing bar
connections in accordance with
the UKAD/EAD (where
applicable)
Provide the corrosion
resistance class required for the
stainless steel used as part of
the post-installed reinforcing bar
connections to be installed into
the structural element and/or its
part in accordance with the
relevant UKAD/EAD, selecting
from Annex A of BS EN
1993-1-4 [Ref 36.N]. Permitted
option limited to: I, II, III, IV, V.
Only applies when stainless
steel bars are specified.
Guidance on the derivation of
the corrosion resistance class is
provided in Annex A of BS EN
1993-1-4 [Ref 36.N].

post installed anchors are to be installed (continued)
Description of structural
element
Provide a description of the
structural element and/or its
part where the post-installed
anchors are to be installed.
This may be the entire
structural element or a part of it.
UKAD/EAD reference(s)
Provide which UKAD/EAD the
post-installed anchors to be
installed into the structural
element and/or its part is to
have a UKTA/ETA issued
against.
Design requirements and
advice on the selection of the
required UKADs/EADs are
given in CD 372 [Ref 20.N].
Temperature range of the
concrete base material in
service in accordance with the
UKAD/EAD
Provide the temperature range,
in accordance with the relevant
UKAD/EAD, of the concrete
base material in service for the
structural element and/or its
part where the post-installed
anchors are to be installed.
Permitted option limited to: T1,
T2, T3.
Design requirements and
advice on the selection of the
required temperature range are
given in CD 372 [Ref 20.N].
Maximum long-term
temperature (Tmlt) and
maximum short-term
temperature (Tmst) of the
concrete base material in
service (where applicable)
Provide the maximum long-term
and the maximum short-term
temperature of the concrete
base material in service, in
accordance with the relevant
UKAD/EAD, for the structural
element and/or its part where
the post-installed anchors are
to be installed.
Only applies when the
temperature range T3 is
specified. The relevant
UKADs/EADs give the option to
specify, in addition to the 'fixed'
T1 and T2 ranges, a bespoke
temperature range (T3) where
the maximum long-term and the
maximum short-term
temperature of the concrete
base material can be chosen,
within specific limits. Further
advice is provided in CD 372
[Ref 20.N].
Compressive strength class of
the concrete base material
Provide the compressive
strength class of the concrete
base material for the structural
element and/or its part where
the post-installed anchors are
to be installed.
This is one of the classes in
Tables 12 and 13 of BS EN 206
[Ref 11.N]and Table A.3 of BS
8500-2 [Ref 13.N]and is the
concrete compressive strength
class of the new or existing
element receiving the
post-installed anchors. As the
relevant UKADs/EADs may only
cater for either a C20/25 or a C
50/60 compressive strength as
representative of a 'low' or 'high'
strength of the base material, in
the subsequent selection of the
product the closest value to the
actual concrete compressive
class specified will be used.

Appendix C. Design outputs for structural concrete
Table C.24 Design outputs for the characteristics of the structural element and/or its part where
post installed anchors are to be installed (continued)
Applicable exposure class
Provide the applicable
exposure class to BS 8500-1
[Ref 12.N]for the structural
element and/or its part where
the post-installed anchors are
to be installed.
Design requirements and
advice on the selection of the
applicable exposure classes for
a structural element and/or its
part are given in Appendix I.
Thickness of concrete base
material
Provide the thickness of the
concrete base material of the
structural element and/or its
part where the post-installed
anchors are to be installed.
Provide value in mm.
This is the depth of the concrete
from the concrete surface in the
direction of the post-installed
anchors to be installed.
Cracked or uncracked concrete
base material to BS EN 1992-4
[Ref 29.N]
Provide whether the concrete
base material of the structural
element and/or its part where
the post-installed anchors are
to be installed is assumed to be
cracked or uncracked in
accordance with BS EN 1992-4
[Ref 29.N].
Permitted option limited to:
cracked, uncracked.
The selection of a cracked or
uncracked condition of the base
material, defined in BS EN
1992-4 [Ref 29.N], affects the
characteristics of the the
post-installed anchor to be
subsequently selected.
Limit/constraint to force(s) to be
applied by the post-installed
anchor(s) to avoid damage to,
or instability of, the structural
element and/or its part
Provide any limit/constraint to
the force(s) to be applied onto
the structural element via the
post-installed anchor(s) to avoid
damage to the structural
element and/or its part.
There may be situations where
the arrangement and/or
ultimate load capacity of the
post-installed anchor(s) lead to
force(s) applied to the structural
element and/or its part which
are higher than the force(s) the
structural element and/or its
part can withstand without
suffering damage or instability.
Providing a limit/constraint to
the force(s) to be applied
ensures that only post-installed
anchors transmitting maximum
forces below such
limits/constraints are used.
Limit/constraint to the concrete
base material hole(s)
diameter/length
Provide any limit/constraint to
the diameter/length of the
hole(s) in the concrete base
material of the structural
element and/or its part where
the post-installed anchors are
to be installed.
There may be situations where
the diameter and/or length of
the hole(s) in the concrete base
material are restricted due to
the specific layout of the
structural element and/or its
part receiving the post-installed
anchor. Providing a
limit/constraint ensures that
only post-installed anchors of
diameter and length within such
limits/constraints are used.

drawing/model within a scheme
showing the structural element
and/or its part receiving
post-installed anchors or
systems for post-installed
reinforcing bar connections
fixings and whose existing
reinforcement is affected by the
drilling.
Relaxation criteria for striking,
damaging or cutting steel
reinforcement
Provide the specific relaxation
criteria on striking, damaging or
cutting existing steel
reinforcement of the structural
element and/or its part affected
by the drilling for installation of
post-installed anchors or
systems for post-installed
reinforcing bar connections, if
different from the default.
The default is no striking,
damaging or cutting of existing
steel reinforcement. However,
specific relaxation criteria may
be provided if calculations
demonstrate that a percentage
of reinforcing bars can be
struck, damaged or cut by
drilling without affecting the
structural capacity. Guidance is
provided in BS 8539 [Ref 9.N].

Table C.26 Design output for relaxation criteria for striking, damaging or cutting of steel
reincorcement within the existing concrete base material and constraints on electrical

Existing steel reinforcement of
dissimilar metal to post-installed
anchor/bar
Provide whether the existing
steel reinforcement in the
structural element and/or its
part is of dissimilar metal to that
specified for the post-installed
anchors and systems for
post-installed bar connections.
Permitted option limited to: yes,
no.
The most common scenario
would be when a stainless steel
anchor/bar is installed into a
reinforced concrete structure
containing carbon steel
reinforcement. A risk of
bi-metallic corrosion exists
where corrosion of carbon steel
in existing concrete structures
has already started or half-cell
readings indicate corrosion may
be imminent, but not where
both carbon and stainless steel
are cast in new concrete in new
construction. Further advice on
use of dissimilar metals for
fixings is given in CD 372 [Ref
20.N], and further advice on the
use of stainless steel bars is
given in Appendix I.
Isolation of dissimilar metals
document reference(s) (where
applicable)
Provide reference of the
document(s) containing the
detailed specification
requirements for the isolation of
dissimilar metals where the
existing steel reinforcement in
the structural element and/or its
part is of dissimilar metal to that
specified for the post-installed
anchors and systems for
post-installed bar connections.
Only applies when the existing
steel reinforcement in the
structural element and/or its
part is of dissimilar metal to that
of the post-installed anchor/bar.
Is/are the unique reference(s)
allocated to every document
where the detailed specification
requirements for the isolation of
the dissimilar metals is given.
The documentation shall clearly
detail the scope, extent and
methods of the isolation of
dissimilar metals and any
specific reporting requirements.
The bonding material in
post-installed reinforcing bar
connections and post-installed
bonded anchors may be used
for the isolation of dissimilar
metals.

Appendix C. Design outputs for structural concrete
Table C.28 Design outputs for type of prestressing of structural concrete (continued)
Drawing/model
reference(s)
Provide reference of drawing(s) or
model(s) where the details of
prestressing in the structural element
and/or its part are shown.
Is/are the unique reference(s)
allocated to every drawing/model
within a scheme showing the
prestressed structural element and/or
its part.
The drawing(s)/model(s) shall include
the arrangement of the pre-tensioning
and/or post-tensioning details.
Design
documentation
reference(s)
Provide reference(s) of the design
documentation for the prestressing of
the structural element and/or its part.
Is/are the unique reference(s)
allocated to every design document
within a scheme associated to the
prestressed structural element and/or
its part and its prestressing system.
The design documentation shall
include any specific design
assumptions and information for the
prestressed structural element and/or
its part that may have an impact on its
production and installation.
Type of prestressing
Provide the type of prestressing of the
structural element and/or its part.
Permitted mutliple option limited to:
pre-tensioning, post-tensioning with
internal bonded tendons,
post-tensioning with internal
unbonded tendons, post-tensioning
with external tendons.
The choice of type of prestressing for
a structural element is derived from
the design. Where a structural
element and/or its part includes more
than one type of prestressing, e.g. a
precast segment post-tensioned with
both internal bonded tendons and
external tendons, both types shall be
listed.
A tendon is considered external when,
after stressing and incorporation into
the works but before protection, it is
outside the concrete section. A
tendon is not considered external
when, for example, a slab comprising
a series of precast beams themselves
stressed with external tendons is
subsequently concreted or grouted in
a way that the prestressing tendons in
the permanent stage are contained in
that filling and achieve the required
cover to reinforcement.
Post-tensioning with external tendons
is assumed to be unbonded by
default; post-tensioning with external
tendons bonded within a concrete
encasement connected to the
structural element is an out of favour
form of post-tensioning where
tendons have limited protection from
corrosion and is not permitted.

Design output / Reference

or notes for design outputs

reference of the structure.
Is the unique reference
allocated to each structure
within a scheme.

Provide the structural element
reference.
Is the unique reference
allocated to each structural
element within a structure
prestressed by pre-tensioning.
Description of structural

Provide a description of the
structural element and/or its part
prestressed by pre-tensioning.

Drawing/model reference(s)
Provide reference of drawing(s)
or model(s) for the structural

Is/are the unique reference(s)

wires and strands for

within the structural element.

deflectors shall have a radius of
no less than 5 times the tendon
diameter for wires, or 10 times
the tendon diameter for strands,
respectively. Also, the angle of
deflection at each deflector shall
not exceed 15°.

reference(s)

accounting for any effects of

but with different strength

use in the same structural
element and/or its part.

reference
Provide the reference of the
pre-tensioning tendon used for
prestressing the structural
element and/or its part.
Is the unique reference
allocated to each pre-tensioning
tendon within a structural
element and/or its part.
Pre-tensioning tendon force to
be applied
Provide the force to be applied
at the jack for the pre-tensioning
tendon, accounting for any
effects of friction. Provide value
in kN.
This is derived from the design.
All pre-tensioning tendons
within a structural element
should be stressed to the same
force; however, also depending
on the tendons size and grade,
the layout of the cross section of
the structural element and the
order of release, that may not
always be the case.
Pre-tensioning tendon
elongation at the applied force
Provide the expected elongation
of the pre-tensioning tendon at
the applied force, accounting for
any effects of friction. Provide
value in mm.
This is derived from the
calculated force/elongation
diagram for the tendon.

compressive strength the
concrete element and/or its part
shall reach before the
pre-tensioning tendons can be
released and the concrete
stressed; this limit is to prevent
overstressing the concrete at
critical sections and comes from
design considerations.
