Appendix C. Design outputs for structural concrete
Drawing/model reference(s)
Provide reference of drawing(s)
or model(s) for the structural
element prestressed by
post-tensioning.
Is/are the unique reference(s)
allocated to every
drawing/model within a scheme
showing the structural element
and/or its part prestressed by
post-tensioning.
The drawing(s)/model(s) shall
include the layout, dimensions
and position of the
post-tensioning tendons and
any other components of the
post-tensioning system,
including the nominal cover to
reinforcement.
When prestressing tendons for
post-tensioning of structural
concrete are deflected within
the structural element, the
deflector shall have a radius of
not less than 50 times the
tendon diameter. Also, the
angle of deflection at each
deflector shall not exceed 15°.
Tendons, whether in anchorage
systems or elsewhere, shall not
pass around sharp bends or
corners as they can provoke
ruptures when the tendons are
under stress.
The anchorage system
comprises the anchorage itself
and the arrangement of
tendons and reinforcement
designed to act with the
anchorage. The form of
anchorage system should
facilitate the even distribution of
stress in the concrete at the end
of the member, and be capable
of maintaining the prestressing
force under
sustained/fluctuating load and
under the effect of shock. No
anchorages shall be placed in
pockets formed in the top
surface of bridge decks;
however, anchorages may be
formed in blisters on the soffit of
bridge deck slabs. Provision
shall also be made for the
protection of the anchorages
against corrosion.
Further guidance is provided in
Hewson, N [Ref 65.I]and CS
TR72 [Ref 35.I].

Appendix C. Design outputs for structural concrete
Table C.30 Design outputs for post-tensioning of structural concrete (continued)
Type of post-tensioning system
Provide the type of
post-tensioning system to be
used for prestressing the
structural element and/or its
part. Permitted multiple option
limited to: internal bonded
tendon with grouted corrugated
plastic duct, internal unbonded
tendon with greased/waxed
smooth plastic duct, internal
unbonded tendon with
individually greased and
sheathed monostrand(s)
with/without grouted smooth
plastic duct, external unbonded
tendon with
grouted/greased/waxed smooth
plastic duct, external unbonded
tendon with individually greased
and sheathed monostrand(s)
with grouted smooth plastic
duct.
Where a structural element
and/or its part incorporates
more than one type of
post-tensioning system, all
types shall be listed.
Protection of external
post-tensioning tendons against
mechanical damage and
corrosion from the atmosphere
or other aspects of the
environment is provided by a
multi-layer system using high
density polyethylene or
polypropylene (for plastic ducts
and sheathing) and grout,
grease or wax.
In determining the type of
post-tensioning system and the
material to be used for the
protection, the design shall take
into account, in addition to the
ultimate and serviceability limit
states analysis and the form of
construction (in-situ, precast,
segmental), any differential
movement between the
structure and the applied
protection that may arise from
changes of load/stress, creep,
relaxation, drying shrinkage,
humidity and temperature.
Whilst in post-tensioning
systems with unbonded
tendons the tendons are often
replaceable (differently from
systems with bonded tendons),
not all unbonded systems
permit tendons to be
retensionable; for example,
external unbonded tendons that
are not individually greased and
sheathed as monostrands and
that are within grouted ducts
rather than within
greased/waxed ducts, are not
usually retensionable.
Further guidance is provided in
Hewson, N [Ref 65.I]and CS
TR72 [Ref 35.I].

Appendix C. Design outputs for structural concrete
Table C.30 Design outputs for post-tensioning of structural concrete (continued)
Protection level for the
post-tensioning tendon to EAD
160004-00-0301 [Ref 61.N]
Provide the required protection
level of the internal/external
post-tensioning tendon in
accordance with FIB Bulletin 75
[Ref 17.I] , FIB Bulletin 97 [Ref
19.I], FIB Bulletin 33 [Ref
16.I]and EAD 160004-00-0301
[Ref 61.N]. Permitted option
limited to: PL2, PL3.
Protection Level 1 (PL1) is
provided by having either
non-encapsulated tendons
(those whose leak tightness of
the anchorage-duct assembly
and of any duct coupler are not
tested) or tendons within steel
ducts, which are not permitted
for use in post-tensioned
highways structures because
experience has shown steel
ducts are prone, in the highway
exposure environment, to
corrosion and therefore do not
offer a reliable protection layer
to the the tendons within.
Protection Level 2 (PL2) is
provided by having
encapsulated tendons within
plastic ducts, whose leak
tightness of the anchorage-duct
assembly and of any duct
coupler are tested. PL2 is the
minimum acceptable level of
protection.
Protection Level 3 (PL3) is
provided by having
encapsulated tendons within
plastic ducts that are also
electrically isolated for the
purpose of in-service
monitoring, and whose
performance of the electrical
isolation of the duct system and
anchorage-duct assembly is
tested. PL3 is an enhanced
level of protection.
Further guidance is provided in
FIB Bulletin 75 [Ref 17.I], FIB
Bulletin 97 [Ref 19.I], FIB
Bulletin 33 [Ref 16.I] and EAD
160004-00-0301 [Ref 61.N].

Table C.30 Design outputs for post-tensioning of structural concrete (continued)
Duct type
Provide the type of duct to be
used in the structural element
and/or its part prestressed by
post-tensioning. Permitted
option limited to: corrugated
plastic, smooth plastic, none.
The type of duct shall be
consistent with the type of
post-tensioning system
specified; some post-tensioning
system types do not have ducts
but only sheathed
monostrand(s).
Further guidance is provided in
FIB Bulletin 75 [Ref 17.I], FIB
Bulletin 97 [Ref 19.I], FIB
Bulletin 33 [Ref 16.I], EAD
160004-00-0301 [Ref 61.N] and
CS TR72 [Ref 35.I].
Duct filling material (where
applicable)
Provide the type of filling
material for the duct to be used
in the structural element and/or
its part prestressed by
post-tensioning. Permitted
option limited to: grout, grease,
wax.
Only applies when ducts are
used in the structural element
and/or its part prestressed by
post-tensioning. The type of
duct filling material specified
shall be consistent with the type
of post-tensioning system
specified.
The type of material to be used
for the protection of tendons in
ducts is derived from the design
and is influenced by factors
such as ultimate and
serviceability limit state
considerations, the form of
construction (in-situ, precast)
and the differential movement
between the structure and the
applied protection that may
arise from changes in
load/stress, creep, relaxation,
drying shrinkage, humidity and
temperature. Further guidance
is provided in CS TR72 [Ref
35.I].
Post-tensioning tendon
reference
Provide the reference of the
post-tensioning tendon used for
prestressing the structural
element and/or its part.
Is the unique reference
allocated to each
post-tensioning tendon within a
structural element and/or its
part.

Appendix C. Design outputs for structural concrete
Table C.30 Design outputs for post-tensioning of structural concrete (continued)
Provision for post-tensioning
tendon to be retensionable in
service required
Provide whether the
post-tensoning tendon used for
prestressing the structural
element and/or its part is
required to be retensionable in
service or not. Permitted option
limited to: yes, no.
This is a design decision and
the choice shall be compatible
with the choice of type of
post-tensioning system,
because not all types of
post-tensioning systems
provide for tendons to be
retensionable in service.
Tendons in bonded
post-tensioning systems are not
retensionable, and only some
types of unbonded
post-tensioned systems provide
for tendons to be retensionable;
for example, external unbonded
tendons that are not individually
greased and sheathed as
monostrands and that are
within grouted ducts rather than
within greased/waxed ducts,
are not usually retensionable.
Further guidance is provided in
CS TR72 [Ref 35.I].
Post-tensioning tendon
replaceability required
Provide whether the
post-tensioning tendon used for
prestressing the structural
element and/or its part is
required to be replaceable in
service or not. Permitted option
limited to: yes, no.
This is a design decision and
the choice shall be compatible
with the choice of type of
post-tensioning system,
because not all types of
post-tensioning systems
provide for tendons to be
replaceable in service.
Tendons in bonded
post-tensioning systems are not
replaceable, whilst in most
unbonded post-tensioned
systems tendons are
replaceable.
Further guidance is provided in
CS TR72 [Ref 35.I].
Post-tensioning tendon force to
be applied
Provide the force to be applied
at the jack for the
post-tensioning tendon,
accounting for any effects of
friction. Provide value in kN.
This is derived from the design.
Post-tensioning tendons within
a structural element may or may
not be stressed to the same
force; this depends on their size
and grade, on the structural
element type and form of
construction, on the layout of
the tendons and their function in
the structural element, and the
order of stressing.

Post-tensioning tendon
elongation at the applied force
Provide the expected
elongation of the
post-tensioning tendon at the
applied force, accounting for
any effects of friction. Provide
value in mm.
This is derived from the
calculated force/elongation
diagram for the tendon.
Order of stressing of
post-tensioning tendons
Provide the order of stressing of
the post-tensioning tendons in
the structural element and/or its
part prestressed by
post-tensioning.
The order of stressing comes
from design considerations and
should minimise eccentric
loading on the prestressed
structural element and/or its
part.
Minimum concrete compressive
strength at transfer before
stressing
Provide the minimum
compressive strength required
for the concrete in the structural
element and/or its part before it
can be stressed by the
post-tensioning tendons.
Provide value in MPa.
This is the minimum
compressive strength the
concrete element and/or its part
shall reach before the
post-tensioning tendons can
stress the concrete; this limit is
to prevent overstressing the
concrete at critical sections and
comes from design
considerations.
Friction coefficients
requirements for tendons and
friction losses at
anchorages/couplings
Provide the values assumed in
design for the friction coefficient
between tendon and
duct/sheathing, any internal
tendon wobble coefficient and
the friction losses at
anchorage/coupling for the
post-tensioning system in the
structural element and/or its
part.
These are derived from the
design, performed in
accordance with BS EN
1992-1-1 [Ref 30.N]and with
reference to 2.2.4 of EAD
160004-00-0301 [Ref 61.N],
where further guidance is
provided.
Minimum radii of curvature
requirements for tendons
Provide the minimum values
assumed in design for the radii
of curvature for any internal
bonded/unbonded and external
unbonded post-tensioning
tendons used for prestressing
the structural element and/or its
part.
These are derived from the
design, performed in
accordance with BS EN
1992-1-1 [Ref 30.N]and with
reference to 2.2.5 and 2.2.6 of
EAD 160004-00-0301 [Ref
61.N], where further guidance is
provided.

Duct fracture resistance testing
to EAD 160004-00-0301 [Ref

Provide the need for testing of
the fracture resistance of duct

limited to: yes, no.

testing, called upon in 2.2.11
and 2.2.12 of EAD
160004-00-0301 [Ref 61.N] for

test used to assess the fracture
resistance of corrugated plastic
ducts for internal bonded
tendons under repeated
loading, whose pass criteria are
considered conducive to ensure
proper tendon encapsulation.

for specifying duct fracture
resistance testing is provided in

Appendix C. Design outputs for structural concrete
Table C.31 Design outputs for steel wires and strands for prestressing of structural concrete
(continued)
Type of steel wire (where
applicable)
Provide the type of steel wire to
BS 5896 [Ref 49.N]in the
structural element and/or its part.
Permitted option limited to: plain,
indented type T1, indented type T
2.
Only applies when the structural
element and/or its part contains
prestressing wires. The choice
between plain and indented wires
is dictated by the fact that they
have different bond characteristics
which result in different design
assumptions to be made, in
accordance with BS EN 1992-1-1
[Ref 30.N], in areas such as
transfer of prestress, wire
anchorage/lapping, minimum
cover to reinforcement for the
transmission of bond, fatigue;
however, there are no differences
between the two indented types in
terms of performance, and the
choice between the two can be
based on wire supply availability,
when known.
Steel designation number
for wire (where applicable)
Provide the steel designation
number to BS 5896 [Ref 49.N]for
the wires in the structural element
and/or its part.
Only applies when the structural
element and/or its part contains
prestressing wires. The steel
designation number is related to
the strength of the wire, and is
therefore a design choice.
Wire nominal diameter
(where applicable)
Provide the nominal diameter to
BS 5896 [Ref 49.N]for the wires in
the structural element and/or its
part. Provide value in mm.
Only applies when the structural
element and/or its part contains
prestressing wires. The specified
wire diameter shall be compatible
with its specified steel designation
number, as not all steel
designations are available for all
sizes.
Type of steel strand (where
applicable)
Provide the type of steel strand to
BS 5896 [Ref 49.N]in the
structural element and/or its part.
Permitted option limited to: 7-wire
strand, indented strand, 7-wire
compacted strand.
Only applies when the structural
element and/or its part contains
prestressing strands. The choice
between plain and indented
strands is a design one mainly
dictated by their different fatigue
performance; compacted strands,
whose tensile capacity is higher
than non-compacted ones due to
their processing and enhanced
cross-section area for the same
strand diameter, are only available
in certain steel designations and
sizes.

Appendix C. Design outputs for structural concrete
Table C.33 Design outputs for duct systems of post-tensioning systems for structural concrete
(continued)
Duct dimensions for-non
circular ducts (where
applicable)
Provide the required outer duct
dimensions when non-circular
ducts are used.
Only applies when non-circular
ducts are specified. When
rectangular or
pseudo-rectangular ducts are
specified, the dimensions of both
major and minor axes shall be
provided. The duct dimensions
should be selected such that the
duct is capable to contain the
required number of tendons.
The cross-sectional area of the
duct should be between 2 and 2.
5 times that of the actual area of
the prestressing tendons.
Further guidance is provided in
FIB Bulletin 75 [Ref 17.I], FIB
Bulletin 97 [Ref 19.I], FIB Bulletin
33 [Ref 16.I], FIB Bulletin 20 [Ref
15.I], FIB Bulletin 7 [Ref 18.I],
EAD 160004-00-0301 [Ref 61.N]
and CS TR72 [Ref 35.I].
Wall thickness of duct
Provide the required wall
thickness of the duct. Provide
value in mm.
The minimum wall thickness of
corrugated plastic ducts used for
internal bonded tendons shall be
2 mm. The minimum wall
thickness of smooth plastic ducts
used for internal unbonded
tendons shall be 2 mm. The
minimum wall thickness of
smooth plastic ducts used for
external unbonded tendons shall
be 4 mm. These values ensure
that plastic ducts are robust for
the loads they are subjected to
from the concrete, the tendons
and external agents.
Further guidance is provided in
FIB Bulletin 75 [Ref 17.I], FIB
Bulletin 97 [Ref 19.I], FIB Bulletin
33 [Ref 16.I], FIB Bulletin 7 [Ref
18.I], EAD 160004-00-0301 [Ref
61.N] and CS TR72 [Ref 35.I].

Appendix C. Design outputs for structural concrete
Table C.33 Design outputs for duct systems of post-tensioning systems for structural concrete
(continued)
Leak tightness of assembled
duct systems test required
Provide the need for performing
a leak tightness test of the
assembled duct systems on site
in accordance with the
procedure in B.5 of Annex B of
FIB Bulletin 75 [Ref 17.I], if
different from the default.
Permitted option limited to: yes,
no.
The default is that leak tightness
testing of the assembled duct
systems is performed, as it is
essential to prove that the duct
systems are encapsulated.
The decision to not require a
leak tightness test should be
based, on a project specific
basis, on the criticality of the
prestressing to the integrity of
the structural element and/or its
part prestressed by
post-tensioning with tendons
within ducts, and of the structure
as a whole. An example where
the leak tightness test can be
omitted is when post-tensioning
with straight ducts/tendons is
used to stiffen a deck
transversely, and failure of the
post-tensioning system does not
lead to ultimate limit state
failures in the structural elements
nor in the whole structure.
Minimum vent internal
diameter
Provide the minimum allowed
internal diameter of the vents, if
different from the default.
Provide value in mm.
The default for the minimum
internal diameter of the vents is
15 mm, a value that ensures
vents can be fitted with valves
capable of being closed and
re-opened to maintain the
pressure during air pressure
testing and to control the flow
during injection of the duct filling
material.
Further guidance is provided in
CS TR72 [Ref 35.I].
Maximum vent spacing
Provide the maximum allowed
spacing for the vents along the
duct, if different from the default.
Provide value in mm.
The default for the maximum
allowed vent spacing along the
duct is 15 m, a value that
ensures the risk of entrapped air
or water in the duct is minimised,
although in cases where the duct
geometry is such that an
enhanced risk of entrapped air
or water in the duct is envisaged
the maximum allowed spacing
may need to be smaller.
Further guidance is provided in
CS TR72 [Ref 35.I].

Appendix C. Design outputs for structural concrete
Table C.33 Design outputs for duct systems of post-tensioning systems for structural concrete
(continued)
Minimum vent height above
highest point
Provide the minimum required
height of the vents above the
highest point of the duct profile,
if different from the default.
Provide value in mm.
The default for the minimum vent
height above the highest point of
the duct profile is 500 mm, a
value that past practice has
shown is enough to ensure
entrapped air and water escapes
from the duct.
Further guidance is provided in
CS TR72 [Ref 35.I].
Distance beyond crests to the
next vent
Provide the horizontal distance
between an intermediate crest of
the duct and the next vent in the
direction of flow of the duct filling
material, if different from the
default. Provide value in mm.
The default for the horizontal
distance between an
intermediate crest of the duct
and the next vent in the direction
of flow of the duct filling material
is the distance from the crest
until the point where the duct is
half its diameter lower than at
the crest, or 1 m, whichever is
the lesser.
Further guidance is provided in
CS TR72 [Ref 35.I].
Vent arrangements at
deviators/diaphragms (where
applicable)
Provide any specific requirement
for the arrangement of the vents
at deviators/diaphragms for duct
systems for post-tensioning
systems with external tendons.
Only applies when
post-tensioning systems with
external tendons are specified.
Specific requirements for the
layout of the vents at
deviators/diaphragms should be
based on previously tried and
tested arrangements, because at
deviators/diaphragms the vents
may, for example, need to have
a diameter and/or be located at a
minimum height smaller than the
default recommended values, for
geometrical constraints.
Further guidance is provided in
CS TR72 [Ref 35.I].

external post-tensioning.
Grout type
Provide the type of grout used for
grouting of the duct in the
structural element and/or its part.
Permitted option limited to: site
batched, pre-bagged.
The grout may be specified as a
proprietary pre-bagged material
where cement and admixtures are
pre-blended and to which only
water is added on site, or as a site
batched blend of cement,
admixtures and water.
Whilst both materials have
identical performance
requirements and are assured by
suitability testing before the actual
grouting operations, the use of
pre-bagged grouts requiring only
the addition of water on site is
recommended as they have more
consistent and reliable properties.
However, for large-scale grouting
operations the use of site batched
grouts can be more practical and
economical.
Further guidance is provided in CS
TR72 [Ref 35.I].
180
Downloaded from https://www.standardsforhighways.co.uk on 12-Nov-2025, CD 350 Version 1.0.0, published: 30-Sep-2025



======================================================================
PAGE 182 of 417
======================================================================
CD 350 Version 1.0.0
Appendix C. Design outputs for structural concrete
Table C.34 Design outputs for grouting of ducts in post-tensioning systems for structural
concrete (continued)
Maximum water/cement
ratio of grout
Provide the maximum permissible
water/cement ratio of the grout
used for grouting of the duct in the
structural element and/or its part, if
different from the default.
Whilst water/cement ratios in the
range of 0.30 to 0.40 can make a
grout achieve the performance
requirements, the default for the
maximum permissible
water/cement ratio of the grout is 0
.35, because high values of the
water/cement ratio increase the
risk of bleeding, segregation and
sedimentation.
The fluidity of the grout during
injection should be high enough for
it to be pumped effectively and to
fully fill the duct, but low enough to
expel the air and any water in the
duct. When the arrangement of the
duct and/or tendons is such that a
high fluidity grout is desirable to
facilitate pumping and duct filling, a
maximum permissible
water/cement ratio of up to 0.40
may be specified. Conversely,
when it is desirable to minimise the
risk of bleeding, segregation and
sedimentation of the grout due to
the layout of the duct being
particularly conducive to the
formation of trapped air at high
points, a maximum permissible
water/cement ratio lower than 0.35
, but no less than 0.30, may be
specified.
181
Downloaded from https://www.standardsforhighways.co.uk on 12-Nov-2025, CD 350 Version 1.0.0, published: 30-Sep-2025

======================================================================
CD 350 Version 1.0.0
Appendix C. Design outputs for structural concrete
Table C.34 Design outputs for grouting of ducts in post-tensioning systems for structural
concrete (continued)
Grout admixture
requirements
Provide the need and reason for a
grout admixture for the grout used
for grouting of the duct in the
structural element and/or its part.
There is no need for specifying a
grout admixture when pre-bagged
grouts, in which cement and
admixtures are pre-blended, are
used; however, when site batched
grouts are used, grout admixtures
may be needed.
Grout admixtures for site batched
grouts can be used to: achieve a
low water/cement ratio and
improve grout compressive
strength without reducing fluidity;
improve fluidity at a given
water/cement ratio; minimise
bleeding at a given water/cement
ratio; ensure volume stability of the
grout; accelerate or retard the set
of the grout, useful when grouting
short or long ducts, respectively.
Depending on the maximum
permissible water/cement ratio of
the grout and the layout of the duct
and/or tendons, single or multiple
grout admixture features above
may need to be specified for the
grout used for grouting of the duct
in the structural element and/or its
part.
182
Downloaded from https://www.standardsforhighways.co.uk on 12-Nov-2025, CD 350 Version 1.0.0, published: 30-Sep-2025



======================================================================
PAGE 184 of 417
======================================================================
CD 350 Version 1.0.0
Appendix C. Design outputs for structural concrete
Table C.34 Design outputs for grouting of ducts in post-tensioning systems for structural
concrete (continued)
Type of grout admixture
(where applicable)
Provide the type of grout admixture
for the grout used for grouting of
the duct in the structural element
and/or its part, such as expanding
in powder form; non-expanding in
powder form; non-expanding in
liquid form; or other.
Only applies when grout
admixtures for site batched grouts
are specified. Grout admixtures
are divided into two types,
expanding and non-expanding,
with both types able to provide the
other property-enhancing features.
Expanding grout admixtures are
supplied as powders which react
with grout constituents to expand
and compensate shrinkage,
ensuring that there is no overall
decrease in the volume of grout at
the end of the hardening period.
Expanding grout admixtures may
be used where the cross-sectional
area of the duct is more than 2.5
times the actual area of the
prestressing tendons, as shrinkage
of the grout is restrained by the
tendons in the duct in a similar
manner to the restraint of concrete
shrinkage in highly reinforced
concrete sections.
Non-expanding grout admixtures
are supplied in liquid or powder
form. It is necessary to explicitly
specify one form or the other only
when it is known that the required
feature of the grout admixture is
provided by one form type.
183
Downloaded from https://www.standardsforhighways.co.uk on 12-Nov-2025, CD 350 Version 1.0.0, published: 30-Sep-2025

======================================================================
CD 350 Version 1.0.0
Appendix C. Design outputs for structural concrete
Table C.34 Design outputs for grouting of ducts in post-tensioning systems for structural
concrete (continued)
Maximum dosage of
admixture (where
applicable)
Provide the maximum dosage of
admixture in percentage by mass
of cement for the grout used for
grouting of the duct in the
structural element and/or its part, if
different from the default. Provide
value in %.
Only applies when grout
admixtures for site batched grouts
are specified.
The default value for the maximum
dosage of admixture in percentage
by mass of cement is 5%, which is
equal to the upper bound for the
dosage of admixtures in concrete
given in BS EN 206 [Ref 11.N].
For grout admixtures, in the
majority of cases the upper bound
of the manufacturer's
recommended dosage range is no
higher than 2-3%, and would
govern. However, there are grout
admixtures for which the upper
bound of the manufacturer's
recommended dosage range
exceeds 5%; hence, this design
output is intended to give flexibility
in the provision of a maximum
dosage to suit specific grout
admixtures requirements.
Grouting pressure range
Provide the minimum and
maximum pressure to be applied
when grouting the duct in the
structural element and/or its part.
Provide a range of values in
N/mm2.
The minimum grout pressure
needed to pump the grout depends
on a number of factors including
the inlet layout, the vertical rise of
the duct and the length of the duct
being grouted, whilst the maximum
pressure should be such as not to
segregate the grout, rupture the
duct, burst the grout inlet, or split
concrete sections. A range of 0.
1-1.0 N/mm2 is consistent with
successful past practice adopted
for highway structures. For very
long ducts, however, the minimum
value of the range may need to be
higher than 0.1 N/mm2, whilst for
vertical ducts the maximum value
of the range may need to be higher
than 1.0 N/mm2.
Further guidance is provided in FIB
Bulletin 20 [Ref 15.I], CS TR72
[Ref 35.I]and Hewson, N [Ref 65.I].
184
Downloaded from https://www.standardsforhighways.co.uk on 12-Nov-2025, CD 350 Version 1.0.0, published: 30-Sep-2025

Appendix C. Design outputs for structural concrete
Table C.34 Design outputs for grouting of ducts in post-tensioning systems for structural
concrete (continued)
Maximum rate of grouting
of the duct
Provide the maximum permissable
rate of grouting of the duct in the
structural element and/or its part, if
different from the default. Provide
value in m/min.
The optimum rate of grouting
depends on a number of factors
including ambient air and grout
temperature, size of duct, amount
of tendons in the duct, duct surface
profile (smooth vs. corrugated),
duct orientation.
In typical longitudinal
post-tensioning ducts with high
and low points, the grout often
flows faster downhill than the
pump provides grout. Hence, it fills
the descending branch of the duct
from the low point backwards and
upwards causing entrapment of air
at the high point, which needs to
be expelled via the vent at that
high point location. To allow this to
happen, the maximum rate of flow
of grout in the duct should be
limited to 10 to 15 m/minute.
The default for the maximum
permissable rate of grouting of the
duct is 10 meters of duct per
minute, which is a conservative
upper limit for grouting of
longitudinal ducts. For vertical
ducts, however, a maximum
permissable rate of 5 m/min should
be specified.
Further guidance is provided in CS
TR72 [Ref 35.I].
Minimum volume of grout
to be expelled at vent
Provide the minimum volume of
grout to be expelled from each
vent during grouting of the duct in
the structural element and/or its
part, if different from the default.
Provide value in litres.
The default is that during grouting
operations, once the fluidity of the
grout flowing from the vents is the
same as the grout being injected, a
minimum of 5 litres of grout at each
vent is vented into a clean
receptacle and discarded.
Higher values may be specified for
very long ducts, ducts with a high
vertical rise or when small size, low
rise vents at deviators/diaphragms
are used.
Further guidance is provided in FIB
Bulletin 20 [Ref 15.I], CS TR72
[Ref 35.I]and Hewson, N [Ref 65.I].
185
Downloaded from https://www.standardsforhighways.co.uk on 12-Nov-2025, CD 350 Version 1.0.0, published: 30-Sep-2025

Appendix C. Design outputs for structural concrete
Table C.34 Design outputs for grouting of ducts in post-tensioning systems for structural
concrete (continued)
Full-scale grouting trials
required
Provide whether full-scale trials of
the grouting operations are
required for the structure and/or
the structural element and/or its
part, if different from the default.
Permitted option limited to: yes,
no.
The default is for full-scale grouting
trials to be performed, as they are
essential to prove that the duct
systems can be grouted
successfully with the grout filling
the ducts and surrounding the
tendons.
The decision to not require
full-scale grouting trials should be
based, on a project specific basis,
on the criticality of the prestressing
to the integrity of the structural
element and/or its part prestressed
by post-tensioning with grouted
ducts, and of the structure as a
whole.
An example where full-scale
grouting trials can be omitted is
when post-tensioning with straight
ducts/tendons is used to stiffen a
deck transversely, and failure of
the post-tensioning system does
not lead to ultimate limit state
failures in the structural elements
nor in the whole structure.

requirements for the grouting
trial.

requirements for the
construction sequence and the
disposal of the grouting trial

Table C.36 Design outputs for designed concrete for structural concrete (continued)
Concrete compressive
strength class
Provide the required
compressive strength class of
the concrete to be used for
concreting of the structural
element and/or its part,
selecting from the classes in
Tables 12 and 13 of BS EN
206 [Ref 11.N]and Table A.3 of

This is selected on the basis of
the required design resistance of
the structural concrete element;
however, the required strength
class of the concrete also
depends on the exposure
conditions and the cover provided
to any reinforcement or tendons.
Compressive strength is specified
by a dual classification where the
characteristic strength of 150 mm
diameter by 300 mm length
cylinders is followed by the
characteristic strength of 150 mm
cubes, e.g. C20/25. BS 8500-1
[Ref 12.N] treats the strength of
concrete measured on 100 mm
and 150 mm cubes as being
identical and therefore in UK the
dual classification applies also to
100 mm cubes.

Appendix C. Design outputs for structural concrete
Table C.36 Design outputs for designed concrete for structural concrete (continued)
Concrete compressive
strength compliance age
Provide the age at which the
compressive strength of the
concrete is evaluated for
compliance with the specified
class for the structural element
and/or its part, if different from
the default. Provide value in
days.
The default compliance age for
compressive strength is 28 days.
The compliance age can be
specified to be earlier or later than
that such as, for example, at 56
days, in doing so permitting the
use of a lower carbon concrete
mix which reaches the required
strength more slowly. However,
when the age of compliance for
compressive strength is specified
to be earlier or later than 28 days,
the implications should be
carefully considered. For
example, when rapid strength
gain is important for the structural
element and/or it part, a concrete
mix with slower strength gain
should not be specified.
When the specified compliance
age is different than 28 days, it
should be required that identity
testing for compressive strength
is undertaken at 28 days in
addition to the compliance age, to
assess compliance with other
specification requirements, such
as for durability and curing, that
are based on a compressive
strength of a concrete mix at 28
days.
Further guidance on using 56
days concrete strengths is
provided in TCC/05/31 [Ref 86.I].
Applicable exposure classes
Provide all the exposure
classes related to the
environmental conditions
relevant for the structural
element and/or its part,
selecting from the exposure
classes in Tables A.1 and A.2
of BS 8500-1 [Ref 12.N].
Design requirements and advice
on the applicable exposure
classes are given in Appendix I.
DC-class (where applicable)
Provide the DC-class for
buried/partially buried concrete
relevant for the structural
element and/or its part,
selecting from the DC-classes
in Table A.10 of BS 8500-1
[Ref 12.N]and including any
adjustment in class as a result
of specifying APM1 (enhanced
concrete quality).
Only applies when the structural
element and/or its part has
concrete buried/partially buried in
ground.
Design requirements and advice
on the selection of the DC-class
are given in Appendix I.

weather, all situations where the
heat of hydration of the mix has to
be controlled to prevent the fresh
concrete having too high of a
differential temperature within it,
that can cause cracking and
curing problems.

Cement compressive strength
class (where applicable)
Provide the required
compressive strength class of
the cement to be used for
concreting of the structural
element and/or its part,
selecting from the classes in
Table 3 of BS EN 197-1 [Ref
6.N] or Table 2 of BS EN
14216 [Ref 7.N] (for very low
heat special cement).
This is not required to be routinely
provided, as it can be selected by
the concrete supplier to be
compatible with the specified
compressive strength class of the
concrete and the specified age of
compliance for the compressive
strength.
However, when specific concrete
mixes, such as those with rapid or
slow strength gain, are required
for the structural element and/or
its part, the compressive strength
class of the cement should to be
specified. When provided, the
cement compressive strength
class needs to be consistent with
the concrete compressive
strength class and the compliance
age for the specified concrete mix.
Loss on ignition for fly ash
(where applicable)
Provide the required category
of loss on ignition for the fly
ash to be used for concreting
of the structural element and/or
its part, selecting from the
categories in 5.2.2 of BS EN
450-1 [Ref 47.N]. Permitted
option limited to: A, B, C.
The selection of the loss on
ignition for fly ash is only required
when fly ash is included in the
concrete mix because a type of
cement (or equivalent
combination) containing fly ash is
specified. Category B is the
default choice, with Category A
specified only when the concrete
mix contains air-entraining
admixtures.
Fineness for fly ash (where
applicable)
Provide the required category
of fineness for the fly ash to be
used for concreting of the
structural element and/or its
part, selecting from the
categories in 5.3.1 of BS EN
450-1 [Ref 47.N]. Permitted
option limited to: N, S.
The selection of the fineness for
fly ash is only required when fly
ash is included in the concrete
mix because a type of cement (or
equivalent combination)
containing fly ash is specified.
Category N is the default choice,
whilst category S may be
specified, due to its enhanced
fineness, when more consistent
performance and strength
enhancement of the concrete mix
and an optimisation of the
water/cement ratio of the concrete
mix via reduced water absorption
are sought.

Provide whether concrete
colouring pigments are
required for concreting of the
structural element and/or its

to: yes, no.
Pigments are required if, for
aesthetic reasons, the structural

designed to have a coloured
concrete surface.
Colour requirements for
pigments (where applicable)
Provide any specific
requirement for the colour of
pigments to be used for
concreting of the structural

be provided to aid selection of the
correct pigments.
Pigment category (where
applicable)
Provide the required category
of the concrete colouring
pigment to BS EN 12878 [Ref
59.N]to be used for concreting
of the structural element
and/or its part. Permitted
option limited to: A, B.
Only applies when coloured
concrete is specified. Category A
should be selected for
unreinforced concrete, and
category B should be selected for
reinforced and prestressed
concrete.

CD 350 Version 1.0.0
Appendix C. Design outputs for structural concrete
Table C.36 Design outputs for designed concrete for structural concrete (continued)
Nominal maximum aggregate
size
Provide the nominal maximum
permitted size of aggregate in
the concrete to be used for
concreting of the structural
element and/or its part, if
different from the default.
Provide value in mm.
20 mm is the default nominal
maximum aggregate size;
however, 10 mm aggregate
should be used for
self-compacting concrete or
where reinforcement is
congested.
Larger aggregate sizes can be
useful to reduce cement demand
and provide a lower carbon
concrete, but they should not be
used in situations where
reinforcement is congested or the
nominal cover to reinforcement is
low. Aggregate sizes larger than
20 mm should be used for
massive structures, such as dams
or very thick sections, and in
these cases 40 mm is the
preferred maximum aggregate
size.
Note that for the selected
intended working life and
specified nominal cover to
reinforcement of a structural
element and/or its part, the
limiting values for the composition
and properties of concrete to
provide the required durability for
each identified exposure class in
Tables A.4 to A.7 and A.9 to A.13
of BS 8500-1 [Ref 12.N]depend
on the nominal maximum
aggregate size specified.
Recycled aggregates
permitted
Provide whether recycled
aggregates, in the form of
coarse crushed concrete
aggregates (CCA), are
permitted in the concrete to be
used for concreting of the
structural element and/or its
part. Permitted option limited
to: yes, no.
The use of recycled aggregates
can help producing a lower
carbon concrete, but this is
typically only justified when
recycled aggregates are available
locally, otherwise the
transportation requirements can
negate any carbon advantages.
Requirements for the use of
recycled aggregates in structural
concrete are provided in CD 374
[Ref 103.N].

Appendix C. Design outputs for structural concrete
Table C.36 Design outputs for designed concrete for structural concrete (continued)
Maximum recycled aggregates
content in percentage by mass
(where applicable)
Provide the maximum
permitted percentage of
replacement, by mass, of the
total amount of coarse
aggregates with recycled
aggregates (coarse CCA) in
the concrete to be used for
concreting of the structural
element and/or its part.
Provide value in %.
Only applies when recycled
aggregates are specified.
Recycled aggregates can have a
detrimental effect on the
properties of structural concrete,
so the permitted percentage
content of recycled aggregates
replacement is limited.
Requirements and advice for the
maximum permitted recycled
aggregates content in structural
concrete are given in CD 374 [Ref
103.N].
Permitted range for the secant
modulus of elasticity in
compression of concrete with
recycled aggregates (where
applicable)
Provide the minimum and
maximum permitted value of
the secant modulus of
elasticity in compression of the
concrete containing recycled
aggregates to be used for
concreting of the structural
element and/or its part.
Provide a range of values in
MPa.
Only applicable when recycled
aggregates are specified.
Recycled aggregates can affect
the modulus of elasticity of the
concrete more greatly than
natural aggregates, leading to a
resulting concrete with a value of
the modulus of elasticity out of the
range typically considered in
design. The modulus of elasticity
of the concrete can significantly
influence design in cases where
deflections, shrinkage and creep
is important, but also in composite
concrete structures where it can
affect the level of the neutral axis
and the stress levels in the
structural element. When
recycled aggregates are
specified, a range of values for
the secant modulus of elasticity
that is compatible with the design
assumptions for the structural
element and/or its part shall be
provided; the subsequent testing
of the concrete containing
recycled aggregates will confirm
whether the actual modulus is
within the range specified.
Further advice is given in CD 374
[Ref 103.N].
Freeze-thaw resisting
aggregates required
Provide whether freeze-thaw
resisting aggregates are
required in the concrete to be
used for concreting of the
structural element and/or its
part. Permitted option limited
to: yes, no.
Guidance is provided in BS
8500-1 [Ref 12.N]and BS 8500-2
[Ref 13.N]. For exposure classes
XF3 and XF4, freeze-thaw
resistant aggregates are required.

Appendix C. Design outputs for structural concrete
Table C.36 Design outputs for designed concrete for structural concrete (continued)
Specific requirements for
aggregate (where applicable)
Provide any specific additional
requirement for the aggregate
in the concrete to be used for
concreting of the structural
element and/or its part.
Where specific properties of
aggregates can have an effect on
concrete characteristics which are
critical for the design assumptions
for the structural element and/or
its part such as strength, density,
shrinkage, creep, moisture
movement, thermal properties,
modulus of elasticity or durability,
specific requirements for the
aggregates shall be specified.
Additional requirements which
may need to be specified include:
requirements and/or constraints
for specific aggregates source;
constraints on special aggregate
type when high strength concrete
is specified; requirements for
aggregates when a high modulus
of elasticity for concrete is sought;
requirements for aggregates with
low coefficients of thermal
expansion to mitigate the adverse
effects of temperature gain within
the concrete in thick sections or in
concretes with high cement
content.
When high strength concrete is
required, and depending on how
high the strength is specified, the
source as well as the type of
aggregate can have a great
influence and special testing of
aggregates may need to be
specified. Further guidance on
high strength concrete is provided
in CBDG TG6 [Ref 53.I].
Further guidance on the
specification of non-lightweight
aggregates to BS EN 12620 [Ref
3.I] and lightweight aggregates to
BS EN 13055-1 2002 [Ref 58.I]in
the UK is provided in PD 6682-1
[Ref 4.I]and PD 6682-4 [Ref 5.I],
respectively.

Appendix C. Design outputs for structural concrete
Table C.36 Design outputs for designed concrete for structural concrete (continued)
Admixture(s) other than
air-entraining required
Provide whether admixtures
other than air-entraining are
required in the concrete to be
used for concreting of the
structural element and/or its
part. Permitted option limited
to: yes, no.
Admixtures for structural concrete
are covered in BS EN 934-2 [Ref
1.N] and BS 8443 [Ref 75.N]and
can serve many purposes
including being water reducing;
plasticizing; superplasticizing;
water retaining; set accelerating;
set retarding; hardening
accelerating; water resisting;
viscosity modifying; shrinkage
reducing; corrosion inhibiting;
segregation reducing; pumping
aiding; underwater concreting
aiding.
Guidance on the need for
specifying admixtures for
structural concrete is provided in
CS TR18 [Ref 1.I].
Type(s) of admixture other
than air-entraining (where
applicable)
Provide the type(s) of
admixture, other than
air-entraining, required in the
concrete to be used for
concreting of the structural
element and/or its part,
selecting from those in Table 1
of BS EN 934-2 [Ref 1.N]and
in clause 4.3 of BS 8443 [Ref
75.N].
Only applies when admixtures
other than air-entraining are
specified. The types of
admixtures available are listed in
BS EN 934-2 [Ref 1.N] and BS
8443 [Ref 75.N], but note that
foaming admixtures and semi-dry
concrete admixtures, covered in
BS 8443 [Ref 75.N], are outside
the scope of use in structural
concrete.
Set retarding admixtures should
only be specified in exceptional
circumstances, for example when
concreting of the structural
element and/or its parts may need
to be undertaken beyond a certain
temperature, typically 30°C.
Further guidance on the selection
of the types of admixtures for
structural concrete is provided in
CS TR18 [Ref 1.I].

Appendix C. Design outputs for structural concrete
Table C.36 Design outputs for designed concrete for structural concrete (continued)
Air-entraining admixture
required
Provide whether air
entrainment is required in the
concrete to be used for
concreting of the structural
element and/or its part.
Permitted option limited to:
yes, no.
When the structural element
and/or it part is subject to
exposure classes relating to the
environmental action of freezing
and thawing (XF), provision of air
entrainment allows, in
accordance with Table A.9 of BS
8500-1 [Ref 12.N], the limiting
values for composition and
properties of concrete to be
relaxed when compared to
concrete without air entrainment.
Air entrainment shall always be
specified when the structural
element and/or its part has a
concrete compressive strength
class C32/40 or lower and is
subject to XF exposure classes.
The carbon contained in fly ash
can substantially reduce the
effectiveness of some
air-entraining agents; for this
reason, when concrete is air
entrained and the concrete mix
contains fly ash, there are
limitations on the category of loss
on ignition of the fly ash specified.

Appendix C. Design outputs for structural concrete
Table C.36 Design outputs for designed concrete for structural concrete (continued)
Minimum air content in
percentage by volume (where
applicable)
Provide the minimum required
air content, by percentage of
air content by volume, in the
concrete to be used for
concreting of the structural
element and/or its part.
Provide value in %.
Only applies when air-entraining
admixtures are specified. The
amount of air entrained in a
designed concrete mix is affected
by many factors, including:
1) Type and amount of
admixture used
2) Consistency of the concrete
3) Concrete proportions
4) Type and grading of the
aggregate
5) The length of time for which
the concrete is mixed
6) Temperature. In the range 10°
C to 30°C, an increase of 10°
C can reduce the amount of
entrained air by 25%
7) The cement type, source,
fineness and cement content
of the concrete.
Guidance on specifying the
minimum required air content,
which is largely dependent on the
aggregate size, is provided in BS
8500-1 [Ref 12.N] and CS TR18
[Ref 1.I].
Fibres required
Provide whether steel fibres to
BS EN 14889-1 [Ref 42.I] or
polymer fibres to BS EN
14889-2 [Ref 41.I]are required
in the concrete to be used for
concreting of the structural
element and/or its part.
Permitted option limited to:
yes, no.
Fibres are permitted only for
non-structural use as defined in
BS EN 14889-1 [Ref 42.I]and BS
EN 14889-2 [Ref 41.I], i.e. when
the addition of fibres is not
designed to contribute to the load
bearing capacity of the element
but only to aid with fresh concrete
mixing and placing, and for
mitigating plastic shrinkage
cracking.
Guidance on the need for
specifying fibres for structural
concrete is provided in CS TR63
[Ref 49.I]and CS TR65 [Ref 50.I].

Appendix C. Design outputs for structural concrete
Table C.36 Design outputs for designed concrete for structural concrete (continued)
Minimum cement content by
mass per concrete volume
Provide the minimum
permitted cement content, by
mass per concrete volume, in
the concrete to be used for
concreting of the structural
element and/or its part.
Provide value in kg/m3.
The minimum permitted cement
content is dependent on strength
and durability requirements. One
of the main characteristics
influencing the concrete durability
is its ability to absorb water. A low
water absorption is achieved by
having a low effective
water/cement ratio, by ensuring
hydration of the cement through
curing and by ensuring maximum
concrete compaction; therefore,
for given aggregates the cement
content should be high enough to
ensure the required consistence
can be reached with a low enough
water/cement ratio, so that the
concrete can be fully compacted.
The selection of the minimum
permitted cement content for the
specified concrete compressive
strength, nominal cover to
reinforcement and maximum
nominal aggregate size is derived
from BS 8500-1 [Ref 12.N] and
BS 8500-2 [Ref 13.N]. Design
requirements and advice on the
selection of the minimum cement
content and its interaction with the
limiting values for concrete
composition and properties in BS
8500-1 [Ref 12.N] in relation with
the applicable exposure classes
are given in Appendix I.
In practice, the actual cement
content used may be greater than
the minimum value specified,
especially when initial testing,
conformity testing and/or
pre-concreting trials indicate that
this is necessary for the
consistent production of a
concrete with a maximum
effective water/cement ratio not
greater than that specified and/or
for special conditions of placing
and compaction.
202
Downloaded from https://www.standardsforhighways.co.uk on 12-Nov-2025, CD 350 Version 1.0.0, published: 30-Sep-2025

CD 350 Version 1.0.0
Appendix C. Design outputs for structural concrete
Table C.36 Design outputs for designed concrete for structural concrete (continued)
Maximum cement content by
mass per concrete volume
Provide the maximum
permitted cement content, by
mass per concrete volume, in
the concrete to be used for
concreting of the structural
element and/or its part, if
different from the default.
Provide value in kg/m3.
The default value for the
maximum permitted cement
content is 550 kg/m3 . A
maximum cement content in
excess of 550 kg/m3 should not
be specified unless special
consideration has been given in
design to the increased creep, the
risk of cracking due to drying
shrinkage in thin sections and
higher thermal stresses in thicker
sections. High strength
lightweight aggregate concrete is
a case where cement contents in
excess of 550 kg/m3 may need to
be specified.
Unless there are specific technical
reasons for the structural element
and or its part subject to
concreting, the maximum
permitted cement content should
be specified to be as low as
possible due to the higher carbon
intensity of concretes with high
cement content.
203

Appendix C. Design outputs for structural concrete
Table C.36 Design outputs for designed concrete for structural concrete (continued)
Maximum effective
water/cement ratio
Provide the maximum
permitted effective
water/cement ratio in the
concrete to be used for
concreting of the structural
element and/or its part.
The maximum permitted effective
water/cement ratio is dependent
on strength and durability
requirements. Low water
absorption, essential to ensure
concrete durability, is achieved by
having a low effective
water/cement ratio. The selection
of the maximum permitted
effective water/cement ratio for
the specified concrete
compressive strength, nominal
cover to reinforcement and
maximum nominal aggregate size
is derived from BS 8500-1 [Ref
12.N] and BS 8500-2 [Ref 13.N].
Design requirements and advice
on the selection of the maximum
effective water/cement ratio and
its interaction with the limiting
values for concrete composition
and properties in BS 8500-1 [Ref
12.N] in relation to the applicable
exposure classes are given in
Appendix I.
Water reducing admixtures can
be beneficial in keeping the
effective water/cement ratio below
the permitted limit.

Appendix C. Design outputs for structural concrete
Table C.36 Design outputs for designed concrete for structural concrete (continued)
Chloride content class
Provide the required chloride
content class for the concrete
to be used for concreting of the
structural element and/or its
part. Permitted option limited
to: Cl 0,10, Cl 0,20, Cl 0,30, Cl
1,00.
The chloride content class sets
out the maximum allowable total
chloride content of concrete for a
given type or use. The chloride
content classes to be specified
shall be:
1) Cl 0,10 for prestressed
concrete (both pre-tensioned
and post-tensioned) and for
heat-cured concrete
containing embedded metal
2) Cl 0,20 for concrete containing
embedded metal and made
with the sulfate-resisting (SR)
cements in Table 1 of BS
8500-2 [Ref 13.N]
3) Cl 0,30 for concrete containing
embedded metal and made
with all other cements in Table
1 of BS 8500-2 [Ref 13.N]
4) Cl 1,00 for concrete not
containing embedded metal
other than corrosion-resistant
lifting devices.
Note that, whilst for
post-tensioned structures for
buildings a chloride content class
of Cl 0,40 is recommended by BS
8500-1 [Ref 12.N], for
post-tensioned bridges and other
highway structures a chloride
content class of Cl 0,10 shall be
specified.

CD 350 Version 1.0.0
Appendix C. Design outputs for structural concrete
Concrete target density
Provide the target density for
the concrete to be used for
concreting of the structural
element and/or its part, taken
in accordance with 5.5.2 of BS
EN 206 [Ref 11.N]for
normal-weight, heavy-weight
or lightweight concrete as
appropriate. Provide value in
kg/m3.
The ranges of target densities are
given in BS EN 206 [Ref 11.N],
with normal-weight concrete
having a oven-dry density ranging
from 2000 to 2600 kg/m3.
When heavy-weight or lightweight
concrete is specified, specific
provisions for the design of the
structural element and/or its part
and for the specification of the
aggregates need to be taken into
account.
Typical aggregates used for
heavy-weight concrete include
heavy natural aggregates such as
barites or magnetite or very heavy
manufactured aggregates such
as iron or lead shot, leading to
densities ranging from as low as 3
500 kg/m3 to as high as 9000
kg/m3 . For heavy-weight
concrete, cement contents and
water/cement ratios are similar to
those for normal-weight concrete
but the aggregate/cement ratios
will be significantly higher,
because of the higher density of
the aggregates. Heavy-weight
concrete can be batched,
transported and placed using
conventional equipment, though
there are obviously certain
aspects, such as the amount that
can be carried by a ready-mixed
truck or handled in a skip, that are
limited by the density. Because of
the higher density, formwork
pressures and the rate of wear of
mixers and pumps are increased.
Compaction may require more
energy than normal-weight
concrete and poker vibrators may
have to be inserted at closer
centres, with a greater tendency
for the mix to bleed.
For lightweight concrete, the
density depends on the type and
grading of the aggregates used,
the moisture content and the mix
proportions.
Further guidance is given in BS
8500-1 [Ref 12.N], BS 8500-2
[Ref 13.N], BS EN 12620 [Ref
3.I], BS EN 13055-1 2002 [Ref
58.I], PD 6682-1 [Ref 4.I]and PD
6682-4 [Ref 5.I], with specific
guidance on lightweight concrete
bridges given in CBDG TG8 [Ref
54.I].
207
Downloaded from https://www.standardsforhighways.co.uk on 12-Nov-2025, CD 350 Version 1.0.0, published: 30-Sep-2025

Appendix C. Design outputs for structural concrete
Table C.36 Design outputs for designed concrete for structural concrete (continued)
Lightweight concrete density
class (where applicable)
Provide the required density
class for the lightweight
concrete to be used for
concreting of the structural
element and/or its part, in
accordance with Table 14 of
BS EN 206 [Ref 11.N].
Permitted option limited to: D1,
0, D1,2, D1,4, D1,6, D1,8, D2,
0.
Only applies when lightweight
concrete is used and a target
density for it is not specified. The
choice of the density class is
derived from the specific design
provisions and from the
specification of aggregates.
Further guidance is given in BS
8500-1 [Ref 12.N], BS 8500-2
[Ref 13.N], BS EN 13055-1 2002
[Ref 58.I], PD 6682-4 [Ref 5.I]and
CBDG TG8 [Ref 54.I].
Consistence class - slump
(where applicable)
Provide the required
consistence class expressed
by slump, in accordance with
Table 3 of BS EN 206 [Ref
11.N], for the concrete to be
used for concreting of the
structural element and/or its
part. Permitted option limited
to: S1, S2, S3, S4, S5.
Only applies to concrete other
than self-compacting concrete.
Slump is the default type of
concrete consistence class that
should be specified. However, for
high workability concrete and stiff
concrete, the flow diameter and
the degree of compactability types
of consistence class, respectively,
should be specified instead of
slump. Slump consistence
classes S2 and S3 are consistent
with successful past practice
adopted for highway structures;
however, the method of placing
can influence the choice, and
higher slump values may be
required for pumped concrete.
Further guidance is provided in
BS 8500-1 [Ref 12.N].

Appendix C. Design outputs for structural concrete
Table C.36 Design outputs for designed concrete for structural concrete (continued)
Target slump (where
applicable)
Provide the target value of the
slump, when tested to BS EN
12350-2 [Ref 101.N], for the
concrete to be used for
concreting of the structural
element and/or its part.
Provide value in mm.
Only applies to concrete other
than self-compacting concrete
and when a target slump value is
specified instead of a slump
consistence class. Where the
level of workability is critical for
the concreting of the structural
element and/or its part, a specific
target value of the slump should
be specified instead of a slump
consistence class. For example,
concrete used for concreting all
new parts of the deck in the
formation of continuity joints
should have a target value of the
slump no higher than 100 mm, as
higher slump concrete mixes are
sensitive to bleeding and
segregation from low-amplitude,
low-frequency vibrations during
the period of setting and early
strength development resulting in
lower bond and compressive
strengths.
Consistence class - degree of
compactability (where
applicable)
Provide the required
consistence class expressed
by degree of compactability, in
accordance with Table 4 of BS
EN 206 [Ref 11.N], for the
concrete to be used for
concreting of the structural
element and/or its part.
Permitted option limited to: C0,
C1, C2, C3, C4.
Only applies to concrete other
than self-compacting concrete.
Slump is the default type of
concrete consistence class that
should be specified. For stiff
concrete, which is however more
common for pavement
construction rather than for use
as structural concrete, the degree
of compactability should be
specified instead of slump.
Target degree of
compactability (where
applicable)
Provide the target value of the
degree of compactability, when
tested to BS EN 12350-4 [Ref
95.N], for the concrete to be
used for concreting of the
structural element and/or its
part.
Only applies to concrete other
than self-compacting concrete
and when a target degree of
compactability value is specified
instead of a degree of
compactability consistence class.
Where the level of workability is
critical for the concreting of the
structural element and/or its part,
a specific target value of the
degree of compactability should
be specified instead of a degree
of compactability consistence
class.

should be specified. For high
workability concrete, however, the

instead of slump.

splitting strength (where
applicable)
Provide the required
characteristic tensile splitting
strength of the concrete to be

strength class.

concrete
Provide the minimum
permitted temperature of fresh
concrete after initial mixing and
prior to placing for the concrete

degrees Celsius (°C).
The default value for the minimum
permitted temperature of fresh
concrete for structural concrete is
5°C. Specification of a different
value should only be under
exceptional circumstances and
upon provision of additional
specific requirements and
constraints for concreting of the
structural element and/or its part
in cold weather.

Appendix C. Design outputs for structural concrete
Table C.36 Design outputs for designed concrete for structural concrete (continued)
Maximum temperature of fresh
concrete
Provide the maximum
permitted temperature of fresh
concrete after initial mixing and
prior to placing for the concrete
to be used for concreting of the
structural element and/or its
part, if different from the
default. Provide value in
degrees Celsius (°C).
The default value for the
maximum permitted temperature
of fresh concrete for structural
concrete is 30°C for CEM I or
CEM II/A or equivalent
combination types, and 35°C for
CEM II/B, CEM II/C, CEM III,
CEM IV or CEM VI or equivalent
combination types. Specification
of a different value should only be
under exceptional circumstances
and upon provision of additional
specific requirements and
constraints for concreting of the
structural element and/or its part
in hot weather.
Requirements for consistence
retention (where applicable)
Provide any requirement for
the consistence retention,
expressed as the minimum
required consistence (by class
or target) for a given
consistence type and for a
specified time after loading at
the mixer, after arrival on site
for delivery or after placing in
the formwork, for the concrete
to be used for concreting of the
structural element and/or its
part.
Consistence retention
requirements should be specified
for self-compacting concrete, for
which maintaining a specific
consistence is particularly
important, but should also be
specified for sites of concrete
placing remote from the concrete
initial mixing; in situations where a
delay in placing is envisaged; to
justify a specific maximum
permitted time delay for placing
fresh concrete against previously
placed concrete; where the
concrete placed is expected to
receive a subsequent pour within
a specific timeframe. This design
output allows to define a level of
consistence (e.g. S3) which
needs to be retained for a given
time (e.g. 2 hours) from a given
point in time (e.g. after loading at
the mixer).
Whilst, as recommended in BS
8500-1 [Ref 12.N], concrete
should by default be placed into
its final position as soon as
practicable to prevent any
unintended loss of consistence,
the provision of specific
requirements for consistence
retention can help to prevent
unacceptable delays in concrete
placing at the construction stage.
Further guidance is provided in
BS 8500-1 [Ref 12.N].

required

to: yes, no.

particularly congested, or in other
situations where vibration of the
freshly placed concrete is
impractical. Guidance is provided
in CS TR62 [Ref 83.I]and Annex
G of BS EN 206 [Ref 11.N].

of self-compacting concrete
(where applicable)

1, SF2, SF3.
Only applies when
self-compacting concrete is
specified.
The slump-flow is the default
mean of assessing the
self-compacting concrete
consistence and should always
be specified.
Guidance is provided in CS TR62
[Ref 83.I]and Annex G of BS EN
206 [Ref 11.N].
Target slump-flow of
self-compacting concrete
(where applicable)

slump-flow of self-compacting
concrete, when tested to BS
EN 12350-8 [Ref 91.I], for the

self-compacting concrete
(where applicable)

[Ref 83.I] and Annex G of BS EN

Appendix C. Design outputs for structural concrete
Table C.36 Design outputs for designed concrete for structural concrete (continued)
Any other requirement and/or
constraint (where applicable)
Provide any other additional
specific requirement and/or
constraint for concreting of the
structural element and/or its
part.
Only applies when there are
additional specific requirements
and/or constraints to be provided.
They include: measures to control
early-age thermal cracking in
accordance to CIRIA C766 [Ref
29.I]; measures to control delayed
ettringite formation; restrictions on
cements/combination types;
special requirements for the
specified APM(s); restrictions on
dosage rates of admixtures;
requirements for the concrete
strength development; specific
requirements for concrete
placing; specific restrictions on
heat development during
hydration; requirements for
resistance to water penetration;
requirements for resistance to
abrasion; site constraints;
limitations on drainage for buried
concrete. CIRIA C766 [Ref
29.I]provides design guidance on
the effects, and control measures,
of restrained thermal and
shrinkage strains in the control of
cracking for structural concrete.
Application of CIRIA C766 [Ref
29.I]requires the use of specific
material and execution
parameters, such as cement
strength class, placing
temperature, formwork type etc.
To avoid imposing unrealistic
constraints on the construction,
for structural elements affected by
restrained thermal and shrinkage
strains any specific requirements
and/or constraints on the
materials and execution
parameters required for the
control of cracking should be
provided as a range of values
based on realistic design
assumptions, rather than as
specific values.

Trial pours for
self-compacting concrete
required
Provide whether trial pours are
required, for the structural element
and/or its part subject to concreting
with self-compacting concrete, to
demonstrate the suitability of the
proposed self-compacting concrete
mix and concreting methods.
Permitted option limited to: yes, no.
Trial pours for self-compacting
concrete are recommended in all
but for very minor and low risk
structural elements, given the
enhanced sensitivity of
self-compacting concrete to
concreting variables such as
admixture dosage rates,
consistence retention, placing rates
and geometry of the structural
element to be cast. Trial pours are
also important to ensure that the
specified concrete finishes are
achieved and that any necessary
controls over the method and rate
of placement can be assessed and
fed back for the permanent works.

relates to.

specified surface finish. The
temperature range is important
because of the sensitivity of
self-compacting concrete to to
the environmental factors
during placing and hardening
with no vibration.

Transparent acrylic windows to
be incorporated into formwork
for the trial pour required
Provide whether transparent
acrylic windows are required to
be incorporated into the
formwork to allow visual
monitoring of the adequacy of
the flow of the self-compacting
concrete during the trial pour.
Permitted option limited to: yes,
no.
Transparent acrylic windows
are recommended for situations
where the layout and density of
the reinforcement and/or the
geometrical features of the
structural element and/or its
part in the permanent works the
trial pour represents are such
that challenges in getting
proper compaction and finish
are expected, and a visual
examination of the flow of the
concrete is beneficial.

transparent acrylic window to be
incorporated into formwork for
the trial pour (where applicable)
Provide the location within the
formwork and the dimensions of
any transparent acrylic window
to be incorporated into the
formwork for the trial pour for
self-compacting concrete.
Only applies when transparent
acrylic windows to be
incorporated into formwork for
the trial pour are specified. The
location and size of the
transparent acrylic windows
shall be such as to permit the
visual monitoring of the areas
where the layout and density of
the reinforcement and/or the
geometrical features pose a
challenge to the flow of the
self-compacting concrete.
Trial pour saw-cuts required
Provide whether any saw-cuts
are required to the hardened
concrete of the trial pour for
self-compacting concrete to
facilitate the visual inspection of
the concrete matrix, if different
from the default. Permitted
option limited to: yes, no.
The default is that trial pour
saw-cuts are required.
However, trial pour saw-cuts
may be omitted where the
layout and density of the
reinforcement and the
geometrical features of the trial
pour are such that a visual
inspection of the hardened
concrete external surfaces is
able to ascertain that the
concrete is free from voids,
honeycombing, segregation,
cracking and other visible
defects.

proper compaction and finish

Appendix C. Design outputs for structural concrete
Table C.43 Design outputs for construction joints in structural concrete (continued)
Construction joint(s) surface
preparation required
Provide the need, due to a
non-prepared surface between
concrete cast at different times
not satisfying the interface
shear requirements of 6.2.5 of
BS EN 1992-1-1 [Ref 30.N], for
the construction joint(s) surface
to be prepared in the structural
element and/or its part
containing the construction
joint(s). Permitted option limited
to: yes, no.
When calculations in
accordance with 6.2.5 of BS EN
1992-1-1 [Ref 30.N] show that,
for a non-prepared (i.e. smooth
or very smooth as defined in 6.2
.5 of BS EN 1992-1-1 [Ref
30.N]) surface between
concrete cast at different times
the interface shear
requirements are met, then
there is no need for a
construction joint surface to be
prepared. Otherwise,
construction
joints are required to be
prepared to provide a 'rough
surface' to 6.2.5 of BS EN
1992-1-1 [Ref 30.N]or,
alternatively, open-mesh
permanent formwork can be
specified.
Open-mesh permanent
formwork for the formation of
construction joints required
Provide the need, due to a
non-prepared surface between
concrete cast at different times
not satisfying the interface
shear requirements of 6.2.5 of
BS EN 1992-1-1 [Ref 30.N], for
the construction joint(s) surface
to have open mesh permanent
formwork for the formation of
construction joints installed in
the structural element and/or its
part containing the construction
joints(s). Permitted option
limited to: yes, no.
Open-mesh permanent
formwork may be used as an
alternative to the preparation of
construction joints, as long as it
provides the required interface
shear resistance at the joint.
Applications of open-mesh
permanent formwork include
the formation of construction
joints in walls and abutments.
Specific requirements for the
construction joint(s)
Provide any specific
requirement for the construction
joint(s) for the structural
element and/or its part
containing the construction
joint(s).
This includes any specific
requirement for the preparation
of the construction joint(s)
surface and its timing, as the
optimum time for treatment is
usually a few hours after
concrete placing; and any
specific requirements for
placing of the new concrete
close to the joint(s), as this
concrete may need to be
particularly well compacted.

Maximum permitted time delay
for placing fresh concrete
against previously placed
concrete
Provide, for the concrete to be
used for concreting of the
structural element and/or its
part, the maximum permitted
delay in placing of a layer of
fresh concrete against a
previously placed layer of
concrete without the need for
the formation of a construction
joint, if different from the default.
Provide value in minutes.
The default maximum permitted
time delay for placing fresh
concrete against previously
placed concrete is 30 minutes,
which is a value ensuring, for all
types of concrete mixes, that a
cold joint is not formed between
layers of concrete placed at
different times (provided that
each batch/load of concrete
placed at different times has
met its specified consistence at
placing).
Higher maximum permitted time
delays than 30 minutes shall
only be provided when the
concrete mix is specified,
together with any other
additional controls, by taking
into account the guidance in
Annex A.9 of BS 8500-1 [Ref
12.N]and requirements for a
consistence retention time and
associated identity testing are
provided.
In cases where it is envisaged
that a specific maximum
permitted time delay cannot be
met at the construction stage
for the placing of a layer of fresh
concrete against a previously
placed layer for the structural
element and/or its part, the joint
between the layers shall be
treated and designed as a
construction joint.
Where, in concrete to be placed at air temperatures below 2°C, a minimum compressive strength of
concrete to be reached before the surface temperature of concrete is allowed to drop below 5°C that is
different from the default value in Table C.45 is required, the design outputs shall be provided in
accordance with Table C.45.

minimum compressive strength of concrete to be reached before the surface temperature of
concrete is allowed to drop below 5°C
Design output / Reference
Information to be provided as
design outputs
Design requirements, advice
or notes for design outputs
The minimum compressive
strength of concrete to be
reached before the surface
temperature of the concrete is
allowed to drop below 5°C.
Provide the required minimum
compressive strength to be
reached by the structural
element before the surface
temperature of the concrete is
allowed to drop below 5°C, if
different from the default.
Provide value in MPa.
This is relevant when concrete
is placed at air temperatures
below 2°C and the temperature
of concrete is initially
maintained at a minimum of 5°
C, before being allowed to drop
only once the concrete reaches
a minimum value of the
compressive strength. The
default is for the required
minimum compressive strength
to be 5 MPa, to avoid damage
from early age freezing.
Deviating from the default and
specifying a lower value, which
may be useful in cases where it
is envisaged that measures to
maintain the surface
temperature of concrete at a
minimum of 5°C may be
impractical given the layout of
the structural element or the
construction stages, shall only
be done where the design is
justified by specialist input and
upon specification of a specific
concrete mix and any additional
controls for cold weather
working.
Where, in concrete to be placed at air temperatures below 2°C, a frequency of measurement of the
surface temperature and determination of the compressive strength of concrete that is different from
the default frequency in Table C.46 is required, the design outputs shall be provided in accordance with
Table C.46.
