Appendix C. Design outputs for structural concrete
Table C.46 Design outputs for, in concrete to be placed at air temperatures below 2°C, the
frequency of measurement of the surface temperature and determination of the compressive
strength of concrete
Design output / Reference
Information to be provided as
design outputs
Design requirements, advice
or notes for design outputs
The frequency of measurement
of the surface temperature and
determination of the
compressive strength of
concrete placed at air
temperatures below 2°C.
Provide the required frequency
of measurement of the surface
temperature and determination
of the compressive strength of
concrete placed at air
temperatures below 2°C, if
different from the default.
This is relevant when concrete
is placed at air temperatures
below 2°C and the temperature
of concrete is initially
maintained at a minimum of 5°
C, before being allowed to drop
once the concrete reaches a
minimum value of the
compressive strength. The
default frequency for measuring
the surface temperature and
determination of the
compressive strength is every
24 hours after concrete placing
and until the compressive
strength reaches the specified
minimum value, with the
strength evaluated using four
specimens made from one
sample for each age of testing
taken randomly, from each
concrete mix, from an amount
of concrete representing no
more than the lesser of 4
batches or 24 m3, but with no
less than one sample per day of
concreting. A higher frequency
may be provided for rapid
strength gain concrete mixes, to
allow early removal of the
measures to maintain the
surface temperature of concrete
at a minimum of 5°C.

Transparent acrylic windows to
be incorporated into formwork
required
Provide whether transparent
acrylic windows are required to
be incorporated into the

monitoring of the adequacy of
the flow of self-compacting
concrete for the structural

Transparent acrylic windows
are recommended for situations
where the layout and density of
the reinforcement and/or the
geometrical features of the
structural element and/or its
part subject to concreting with
self-compacting concrete are
such that challenges in getting
proper compaction and finish
are expected and a visual
examination of the flow of the
concrete is beneficial.

to be incorporated into the
formwork for the structural
element and/or its part subject
to concreting with
self-compacting concrete.
Only applies when transparent
acrylic windows to be
incorporated into formwork are
specified. The location and size
of the transparent acrylic
windows shall be such as to
permit the visual monitoring of
the areas where the layout and
density of the reinforcement
and/or the geometrical features
pose a challenge to the flow of
the self-compacting concrete.

Appendix C. Design outputs for structural concrete
Table C.48 Design outputs for the compaction of fresh concrete for structural concrete
(excluding self-compacting concrete)
Design output / Reference
Information to be provided as
design outputs
Design requirements, advice
or notes for design outputs
The time limit of undertaking
recompaction of upper layers of
deep lifts in concrete
installations to prevent
settlement cracking following
intial compaction
Provide an upper and lower
limit for the time, after initial
compaction, within which
recompaction of upper layers of
deep lifts can be undertaken.
Provide a range of values in
hours.
Recompaction of fresh concrete
should not be undertaken after
initial compaction, and fresh
concrete should not be
disturbed for 24 hours after
initial compaction.
However, in deep concrete
pours the upper layers can be
susceptible to settlement
cracking caused by water gain
from below, and recompaction
may be useful to prevent or
anneal settlement cracking; a
window of time within which
recompaction is allowed should
be provided for such cases.
Guidance is provided in CS
TR22 [Ref 61.I]and CS GCG8
[Ref 48.I].

Appendix C. Design outputs for structural concrete
Curing class
Provide the curing class, in
accordance with Table 4 of BS
EN 13670 [Ref 45.N], to be
assumed for the concrete to be
used for concreting of the
structural element and/or its part,
if different from the default.
Permitted option limited to: 1, 2,
3, 4.
The duration of curing is
dependent on the development
of the concrete properties in the
surface zone and is determined
via the specification of a curing
class, taken from those given in
Table 4 of BS EN 13670 [Ref
45.N]and defined by a curing
period or a percentage of the
specified characteristic 28 day
compressive strength reached by
concrete surface after a certain
duration of curing. Methods of
estimating the development of
concrete properties in the surface
zone are given in Annex F of BS
EN 13670 [Ref 45.N], whilst
Tables F.2 to F.4 of BS EN 13670
[Ref 45.N] give the minimum
duration of curing for curing
classes 2 to 4 as a function of the
concrete strength development.
Information on the strength
development of the concrete
used for concreting the structural
element and /or its part, which is
required at the construction stage
to derive the required minimum
duration of curing for any
specified curing class, can be
provided by the concrete
producer, in accordance with
Clause 7.2 of BS EN 206 [Ref
11.N] and Clause 7.1 of BS
8500-2 [Ref 13.N].
The default curing class is 3, that
is consistent with successful past
practice adopted for highway
structures, and means curing is
continued until the surface of the
concrete has reached 50% of its
specified 28 day compressive
strength (or 50% of its estimated
28 day compressive strength, if
the concrete compliance age for
the structural element and/or its
part is not 28 days).
A lower curing class may be
specified in exceptional
circumstances to suit the timeline
of specific construction stages for
the works; conversely, a higher
curing class may be specified
when the significance of curing is
particularly important to assure
the strength, crack control,
durability and aesthetics of the
structural element and/or its part.
The effect of any specified
admixtures on a specific curing

Appendix C. Design outputs for structural concrete
Table C.49 Design outputs for curing of concrete for structural concrete (continued)
Accelerated curing via
elevated-temperature curing
required
Provide whether accelerated
curing via elevated-temperature
curing is required for the concrete
to be used for concreting of the
structural element and/or its part.
Permitted option limited to: yes,
no.
Accelerated curing, of which only
elevated-temperature curing (the
most common being steam
curing) is permitted, consists of
curing the concrete in an
environment in which the
humidity and the rate of
temperature rise and fall are
controlled, to speed up the rate
of increase in strength. Further
guidance on the need of
specifying accelerated curing is
provided in CS CA20 [Ref 25.I].
Additional special curing
requirements
Provide any additional special
curing requirements for the
concrete to be used for
concreting of the structural
element and/or its part.
This includes any requirement for
information on concrete strength
development to be provided, and
any other requirements such as
special provisions to mitigate
against plastic shrinkage
cracking when high strength
concrete and self-compacting
concrete is specified, or when
concreting in hot weather, cold
weather, windy or dry air
conditions. Further design
requirements, advice and
guidance on the provision of
additional special curing
requirements are given in
Appendix I and CS CA20 [Ref
25.I].

Appendix C. Design outputs for structural concrete
Table C.50 Design outputs for formed surface finish for structural concrete (continued)
Special requirements for
formed surface finish (where
applicable)
Provide any special
requirement for the formed
surface finish for the structural
element and/or its part,
including specific formed
surface finish requirement when
a class other than F1 to F5 is
specified.
Only applies when a formed
surface finish class other than
F1 to F5 is specified. Special
requirements include any finish
that requires the coarse
aggregate to be permanently
exposed; the use of special
forms or linings to provide a
specific texture; the use of a
different concrete mix near the
surface; the need for grinding,
bush-hammering or other
treatment. Formed surface
finish for a class other than F1
to F5 should be related to
samples that are readily
available for comparison.
Positions, other than rebates,
where internal ties are
permitted for class F4 finish
(where applicable)
Provide the positions, other
than rebates, where internal
ties are permitted for class F4
finish in the structural element
and/or its part with formed
surface finish.
Only applies when surface
finish class F4 is specified.
The default is for surface finish
class F4 to have internal ties
only in rebates, but there can
be exceptions. Although metal
parts should never be
permanently embedded within
the cover depth from the
surface of the concrete, internal
ties can be used in ways which
will not detract from the
appearance. For instance, if
made coincident with certain
types of surface features, such
as vertical grooves formed to
break up large areas or features
which create shadow effects,
the holes are practically
indiscernible and an economical
design of formwork ensues.
Requirements for special
protection of formed surface
finish (where applicable)
Provide, for the structural
element and/or its part, any
requirement for special
protection of formed surface
finish that is vulnerable to
damage.
Only applies when temporary
protection is required for the
formed surface finish. High
quality formed surface finishes,
such as F3, F4, F5 and any
special finish classes, can be
susceptible to damage and
temporary protection may be
required. Further guidance is
provided in CS TR52 [Ref
63.I]and CS 171 [Ref 95.I].
Where unformed surface finish for structural concrete is required, the design outputs shall be provided
in accordance with Table C.51.

construction

on the construction of the deck
widening.

include limiting traffic speed;
provision of weight restrictions;
provision of temporary vehicle
restraint systems; specific
requirements for temporary
works or supports.

Appendix C. Design outputs for structural concrete
Table C.52 Design outputs for continuity joints in bridge decks of structural concrete (continued)
Locations of deflection and
vibration measurement points
along the interface
Provide where, along the
interface between the existing
and new parts of the deck, any
deflection and vibration
measurement points are to be
located for the structural
element and/or its part being
widened, built in stages or
reconstructed in stages with
continuity joints, also with
reference to the
drawing(s)/model(s).
This is derived by the design
and is influenced, amongst
other parameters, by the type of
bridge deck widening
construction, bridge articulation
and span length. The
measurement points shall be
located at the interface between
the existing trafficked deck and
the new part of the deck
attached directly to it, or at the
interface between the existing
deck and the in-fill strip when
the in-fill strip method of
construction is used. Along
each interface to be measured,
the number and location of
measurement points should be
such that the highest values of
the differential deflection and/or
vibration are captured for the
structural element and/or its
part.
Further design requirements
and advice on deflection and
vibration measurements are
given in CD 364 [Ref 48.N].
Minimum accuracy of deflection
and vibration measurements
Provide the minimum accuracy
required in the measurement of
deflections and vibrations along
the interface between the
existing and new parts of the
deck for the structural element
and/or its part being widened,
built in stages or reconstructed
in stages with continuity joints.
The default is that the minimum
accuracy required in the
measurement of deflections
and vibrations shall be to within
10% of the respective
measurement accuracy limits.
Calibration requirements for
deflection and vibration
measurement equipment
Describe any specific
requirement for the calibration
of equipment to be used for
measuring deflections and
vibrations along the interface
between the existing and new
parts of the deck, for the
structural element and/or its
part being widened, built in
stages, or reconstructed in
stages with continuity joints.
The default requirement is that
deflection and vibration
measurement equipment shall
be calibrated at a frequency in
accordance with the
manufacturer's instructions, but
no more than 4 weeks prior to
its use in the works.

Appendix C. Design outputs for structural concrete
Table C.52 Design outputs for continuity joints in bridge decks of structural concrete (continued)
Requirements for competency
of personnel undertaking
deflection and vibration
measurements
Provide any requirement for the
competency of personnel
undertaking deflection and
vibration measurements along
the interface between the
existing and new parts of the
deck for the structural element
and/or its part being widened,
built in stages or reconstructed
in stages with continuity joints.
This is to mitigate the risk of
inaccurate results being
provided by personnel
undertaking deflection and
vibration measurements not
qualified or experienced in the
use of the measuring
equipment.
Where a target value of slump of the concrete used for concreting all new parts of the deck in the
formation of the continuity joint that is different from the default value in Table C.53 is required, the
design outputs shall be provided in accordance with Table C.53.
Table C.53 Design outputs for the target value of slump of the concrete used for concreting all
new parts of the deck in the formation of the continuity joint
Design output / Reference
Information to be provided as
design outputs
Design requirements, advice
or notes for design outputs
The target value of the slump of
the concrete used for concreting
all new parts of the deck in the
formation of the continuity joint
Provide the target value of the
slump of the concrete used for
concreting all new parts of the
deck in the formation of the
continuity joint, if different from
the default. Provide value in
mm.
The default is for the concrete
used for concreting all new
parts of the deck to have a
target value of the slump of 100
mm, as higher slump concrete
mixes are sensitive to bleeding
and segregation from low
amplitude, low frequency
vibrations during the period of
setting and early strength
development, resulting in lower
bond and compressive
strengths.
When justified by specialist
input in relation to the specified
concrete mix, method of placing
and any requirements and
constraints on the deck
widening construction, a
different value may provided.
Whilst is it not recommended to
specify a target value of the
slump higher than 100 mm,
lower target values than 100
mm may be specified to
minimise bleeding and
segregation provided any
adverse implications on the
workability of the concrete mix
are mitigated.
Further advice is provided in
CD 364 [Ref 48.N].

Appendix C. Design outputs for structural concrete
Table C.54 Design outputs for, in the formation of continuity joints in bridge decks of structural
concrete, the frequency of determination of the compressive strength of concrete and/or of
measurement of the differential deflection/vibration at the interface (continued)
The frequency of determination
of the compressive strength of
the concrete in the separate
parallel deck (where applicable)
Provide the required frequency
of compressive strength testing
of the concrete in the separate
parallel deck before the second
stage in-fill strip can be
constructed, if different from the
default.
Only applies when the in-fill
strip method of construction is
used in the formation of
continuity joints.
The default is testing
specimens at 14 days after
concrete placing and thereafter
every 24 hours until the
compressive strength reaches
the value corresponding to the
compressive strength class
specified for the separate
parallel deck, with the
compressive strength evaluated
from two test specimens made
from one sample for each age
of testing taken randomly from
an amount of concrete
representing no more than the
lesser of 4 batches or 24 m3,
but with no less than one
sample per day of concreting.
This acknowledges the fact that
the in-fill strip, built as a second
stage after the first stage
separate parallel deck, should
not be constructed until the
compressive strength class
specified for the separate
parallel deck is reached, and in
any case no earlier than 14
days after placing of the
concrete in the separate
parallel deck to cater for the
strength development of
different concrete mixes - but it
gives the flexibility to be able to
provide a more or less stringent
testing regime and timeline, for
example to suit the timeline of
specific construction stages for
the works; traffic management
restrictions; hot/cold weather
working; the use of concrete
with rapid/slow setting time.
Further advice is provided in
CD 364 [Ref 48.N].

The frequency of determination
of the compressive strength of
the concrete in the new part of
the deck or in the in-fill strip with
the purpose of justifying the
duration of measurement of the
differential deflection at the
interface (where applicable)
Provide the required frequency
of compressive strength testing
of the concrete in the new part
of the deck or in the in-fill strip
with the purpose of justifying
the duration of measurement of
the differential deflection at the
interface, if different from the
default.
Only applies when the
formation of continuity joints is
via a new part of the deck
attached directly to the existing
trafficked deck, or via the in-fill
strip method of construction
with traffic running less than 1
m from the interface between
the existing trafficked deck and
the concrete in-fill strip; in
accordance with CD 364 [Ref
48.N], there is no need to
measure differential deflections
when the in-fill strip method of
construction is used with traffic
running 1 m or more from the
interface between the existing
trafficked deck and the concrete
in-fill strip.
The default is testing
specimens at 3 and 7 days after
concrete placing, and thereafter
every 24 hours until the
compressive strength reaches
the value corresponding to the
compressive strength class
specified for the new part of the
deck or the in-fill strip, with the
compressive strength evaluated
from two test specimens made
from one sample for each age
of testing taken randomly from
an amount of concrete
representing no more than the
lesser of 4 batches or 24 m3,
but with no less than one
sample per day of concreting.
This acknowledges the fact
that, to mitigate the risk of
defects at the interface, the
differential deflection should be
measured until the compressive
strength class specified for the
new part of the deck or the in-fill
strip deck is reached, and in
any case for no less than 7
days after placing of the
concrete in the new part of the
deck or in the in-fill strip to cater
for the strength development of
different concrete mixes - but it
gives the flexibility to be able to
provide a more or less stringent
testing regime and timeline, for
example to suit the timeline of
specific construction stages for
the works; traffic management
restrictions; hot/cold weather
working; the use of concrete
with rapid/slow setting time.

Appendix C. Design outputs for structural concrete
Table C.54 Design outputs for, in the formation of continuity joints in bridge decks of structural
concrete, the frequency of determination of the compressive strength of concrete and/or of
measurement of the differential deflection/vibration at the interface (continued)
The frequency of measurement
of the differential deflection at
the interface between the
existing trafficked deck and the
new part of the deck or at the
interface between the existing
trafficked deck and the in-fill
strip (where applicable)
Provide the required frequency
of measurement of the
differential deflection at the
interface between the existing
trafficked deck and the new part
of the deck or at the interface
between the existing trafficked
deck and the in-fill strip, if
different from the default.
Only applies when the
formation of continuity joints is
via a new part of the deck
attached directly to the existing
trafficked deck, or via the in-fill
strip method of construction
with traffic running less than 1
m from the interface between
the existing trafficked deck and
the concrete in-fill strip; in
accordance with CD 364 [Ref
48.N], there is no need to
measure differential deflections
when the in-fill strip method of
construction is used with traffic
running 1 m or more from the
interface between the existing
trafficked deck and the concrete
in-fill strip.
The default is measuring the
differential deflection
continuously, commencing
immediately after placing of the
concrete in the new part of the
deck or in the in-fill strip and
continued until the compressive
strength of the concrete of the
new part of the deck or the in-fill
strip reaches the value
corresponding to the
compressive strength class
specified or until 7 days after
concrete placing, whichever is
later.
Any more or less stringent
differential deflection
measurement regime and
timeline (for example to suit the
timeline of specific construction
stages for the works; traffic
management restrictions;
hot/cold weather working; the
use of concrete with rapid/slow
setting time) shall be compatible
with any deviation from the
default specified for the related
frequency of compressive
strength testing of the concrete.
Further advice is provided in
CD 364 [Ref 48.N].

Appendix C. Design outputs for structural concrete
Table C.54 Design outputs for, in the formation of continuity joints in bridge decks of structural
concrete, the frequency of determination of the compressive strength of concrete and/or of
measurement of the differential deflection/vibration at the interface (continued)
The frequency of determination
of the compressive strength of
the concrete in the new part of
the deck or in the in-fill strip with
the purpose of justifying the
duration of measurement of the
vibration at the interface
Provide the required frequency
of compressive strength testing
of the concrete in the new part
of the deck or in the in-fill strip
with the purpose of justifying
the duration of measurement of
the vibration at the interface, if
different from the default.
The default is testing
specimens at 3 and 7 days after
concrete placing, and thereafter
every 24 hours until the
compressive strength reaches
the value corresponding to the
compressive strength class
specified for the new part of the
deck or the in-fill strip, with the
compressive strength evaluated
from two test specimens made
from one sample for each age
of testing taken randomly from
an amount of concrete
representing no more than the
lesser of 4 batches or 24 m3,
but with no less than one
sample per day of concreting.
This acknowledges the fact
that, to mitigate the risk of
reduced anchorage bond due to
the reinforcement moving
relative to the immature
concrete causing cracks in the
concrete which can be filled
with weak diluted grout, the
vibration should be measured
until the compressive strength
class specified for the new part
of the deck or the in-fill strip
deck is reached, and in any
case for no less than 7 days
after placing of the concrete in
the new part of the deck or in
the in-fill strip to cater for the
strength development of
different concrete mixes - but it
gives the flexibility to be able to
provide a more or less stringent
testing regime and timeline, for
example to suit the timeline of
specific construction stages for
the works; traffic management
restrictions; hot/cold weather
working; the use of concrete
with rapid/slow setting time.
Further advice is provided in
CD 364 [Ref 48.N].

default.

to be implemented at the
construction stage to reduce
the vibrations below the
specified limits before
proceeding with the works.

vibration measurement regime
and timeline (for example to suit
the timeline of specific
construction stages for the
works; traffic management
restrictions; hot/cold weather
working; the use of concrete
with rapid/slow setting time)
shall be compatible with any
deviation from the default
specified for the related
frequency of compressive
strength testing of the concrete.

CD 350 Version 1.0.0
Appendix C. Design outputs for structural concrete
Table C.55 Design outputs for identity testing of structural concrete (continued)
Point of sampling for identity
testing of structural concrete
(except for consistence
retention)
Provide the required point
where the samples for the
concrete used for concreting of
the structural element and/or its
part subject to identity testing
are to be taken, if different from
the default.
Concrete samples to be used
for identity testing may be taken
at the point of placing of the
concrete into the formwork; at
the point of discharge of the
concrete from the producer's
delivery vehicle; at the mixer; or
at any other required location.
For concrete mixed on site and
for precast concrete where
ready-mixed concrete is not
used, the default is for the
samples to be taken at the point
of placing into the formwork; for
ready-mixed concrete and for
precast concrete where
ready-mixed concrete is used,
the default is for the samples to
be taken at the point of
discharge from the producer's
delivery vehicle.
For ready-mixed concrete,
specifying the point of sampling
to be at discharge from the
producer's delivery vehicle or at
the mixer (in cases where the
concrete is delivered into the
user's vehicle) means that the
results from identity testing
represent the concrete 'as
delivered'; however, when it is
important to ensure that identity
testing represents the concrete
'as placed' into the works, for
example in situations where the
distance between discharge
and placing is expected to be
large or when concrete is to be
pumped, the point of sampling
should be specified as the point
of placing into the formwork, or
specific consistence retention
requirements should be
specified. The choice of the
point of sampling also depends
on the type(s) of identity testing
to be performed.
Further guidance is provided in
BS 8500-1 [Ref 12.N]and BS
8500-2 [Ref 13.N].

Appendix C. Design outputs for structural concrete
Required type(s) of identity
testing for fresh concrete
(where applicable)
Provide the type(s) of identity
testing for fresh concrete to be
performed on the concrete used
for concreting of the structural
element and/or its part.
Permitted multiple option limited
to: slump, degree of
compactability, flow, slump-flow
(of self-compacting concrete),
viscosity t500 (of self compacting
concrete), viscosity tv (of
self-compacting concrete),
passing ability L-box (of self
compacting concrete), passing
ability J-ring (of self-compacting
concrete), segregation
resistance (of self-compacting
concrete), air content, density
of fresh concrete, homogeneity
of fibre distribution, effective
water/cement ratio, consistence
retention.
Only applies when at least one
type of identity testing for fresh
concrete is required for the
concrete used for concreting of
the structural element and/or its
part. The purpose of identity
testing is to check whether the
concrete properties of a specific
batch of concrete, from which
samples are taken at the point
of sampling, are in compliance
with the concrete properties
specified for the structural
element and/or its part being
executed with the concrete
whose batch the samples are
taken from. The need for
identity testing should be
matched to the use and
criticality of the structural
element and/or its part.
Identity testing for fresh
concrete should be specified
when the compressive strength
class of the concrete mix used
for concreting of the structural
element and/or its part is C25/3
0 or greater. Identity testing for
fresh concrete shall always be
specified for cantilevers, end
blocks, half-joints, highly
stressed areas, self-compacting
concrete, concrete containing
fibres, air-entrained concrete,
concrete containing recycled
aggregates and when the
compressive strength class of
the concrete mix used for
concreting of the structural
element and/or its part is
greater than C50/60.
The type(s) of identity testing
for fresh concrete should be all
those related to the fresh
concrete properties specified
for the structural element and/or
its part the identity testing refers
to, with the exception that
identity testing for density of
fresh concrete should only be
specified for lightweight
concrete, heavy-weight
concrete or when the weight of
the concrete is particularly
important for the design.
Identity testing for homogeneity
of fibre distribution should be
specified when fibres are used
in the concrete used for
concreting of the structural
l
d/
i

Appendix C. Design outputs for structural concrete
Table C.55 Design outputs for identity testing of structural concrete (continued)
Required type(s) of identity
testing for hardened concrete
(where applicable)
Provide the type(s) of identity
testing for hardened concrete to
be performed on the concrete
used for concreting of the
structural element and/or its
part. Permitted multiple option
limited to: concrete
compressive strength, density
of hardened concrete, secant
modulus of elasticity in
compression of hardened
concrete.
Only applies when at least one
type of identity testing for
hardened concrete is required
for the concrete used for
concreting of the structural
element and /or its part.
Identity testing for hardened
concrete should be specified
when the compressive strength
class of the concrete mix used
for concreting of the structural
element and/or its part is C25/3
0 or greater. Identity testing for
hardened concrete shall always
be specified for cantilevers, end
blocks, half-joints, highly
stressed areas, self-compacting
concrete, concrete containing
fibres, air-entrained concrete,
concrete containing recycled
aggregates and when the
compressive strength class of
the concrete mix used for
concreting of the structural
element and/or its part is
greater than C50/60.
The type(s) of identity testing for
hardened concrete should be all
those related to the hardened
concrete properties specified
for the structural element and/or
its part the identity testing refers
to, with the exception that
identity testing for density of
hardened concrete should only
be specified for lightweight
concrete, heavy-weight
concrete or when the weight of
the concrete is particularly
important for the design, and
identity testing for secant
modulus of elasticity in
compression of hardened
concrete should only be
specified when the design can
be particularly sensitive to the
elastic modulus, such as in
prestressed concrete and
where recycled aggregates are
used.

Appendix C. Design outputs for structural concrete
The frequency of determination
of the compressive strength of
concrete in the hardened state
for a reinforced concrete
structural element (where
applicable)
Provide the required frequency
of compressive strength testing
of concrete in the hardened
state for identity testing of a
reinforced concrete structural
element, if different from the
default.
Only applies when the
structural element is made of
reinforced concrete and when
identity testing for the
compressive strength of
concrete in the hardened state
is required, from Table C.55, for
the concrete used for
concreting of the structural
element and or its part.
The default frequency is testing
four test specimens made from
one sample taken randomly, for
each concrete mix, from an
amount of concrete
representing no more than the
lesser of 4 batches or 24 m3,
but with no less than one
sample taken per day of
concreting, and tested at 28
days.
For large schemes where
construction is expected to last
for several months or years,
higher rates of sampling/testing
should be specified for the start
of the works, to be then relaxed
once there is confidence in the
consistency of the results.
Conversely, it should be
specified that the rates of
sampling/testing are increased
when a given proportion of
non-compliant results are
obtained.
For cantilevers, end blocks,
half-joints, highly stressed
areas and when the
compressive strength class of
the concrete mix used for
concreting of the structural
element and/or its part is
greater than C50/60, the rates
of sampling/testing should be
equal to those recommended
for prestressed concrete in this
Table.
When an innovative or very
high strength concrete mix is
used and and in any situation
where doubts on strength
development or a higher risk of
non-compliance with the
compressive strength
requirements exist, a number of
samples higher than the default
should be specified with the
purpose of having spare
specimens to be tested at test
ages other than 28 days.

reference of the structure.

reference

element(s) or a part of it/them.

Drawing/model reference(s)
Provide reference of drawing(s)
or model(s) for the precast

and any in-situ concrete

drawing/model within a scheme
showing the precast concrete

element and/or its part
connected to it.

preparation, installation and
positional restraint
requirements for the precast
concrete element; any other
specific information necessary
to manufacture the product,
including requirements and
criteria for prestressing and
rebates to accommodate
permanent soffit formwork.

reference(s)

Appendix C. Design outputs for structural concrete
Table C.58 Design outputs for requirements for precast structural concrete (continued)
Precast concrete element within
the scope of a designated
precast concrete product
standard
Provide whether the precast
concrete element is in the
scope of a designated precast
concrete product standard.
Permitted option limited to: yes,
no.
All precast concrete elements
to be used in the works that fall
within the scope of a designated
precast concrete product
standard shall be in accordance
with that standard. Designated
precast concrete product
standards relevant to highway
structures include BS EN 12843
[Ref 64.N]for masts and poles;
BS EN 14844 [Ref 62.N]for box
culverts; BS EN 15050 [Ref
63.N]for bridge deck elements;
BS EN 15258 [Ref 65.N]for
retaining wall elements.
However, designated precast
concrete product standards do
not cover all the structural
element types found in
highways structures; for
example, bridge piers, columns
and abutments are not in the
scope of any designated
precast concrete product
standard.
Note that BS EN 13369 [Ref
10.N], which covers common
rules for precast concrete
products and may be used for
any type of precast concrete
element, is not a designated
standard.
Reference standard for the
manufacturing of the precast
concrete element within the
scope of a designated precast
concrete product standard
(where applicable)
Provide the designated precast
product standard the precast
concrete element is to be
manufactured to. Permitted
option limited to: BS EN 12843
[Ref 64.N], BS EN 14844 [Ref
62.N], BS EN 15050 [Ref 63.N],
BS EN 15258 [Ref 65.N].
Only applies when the precast
concrete element falls within the
scope of a designated precast
concrete product standard.
The designated standard
relevant for the precast
concrete element in object shall
be selected as design output.
Note that the list of options
excludes designated precast
product standards for piles and
embedded retaining walls,
which are in the scope of CC
602 [Ref 60.N]and not of CC
482 [Ref 91.N].

Table C.58 Design outputs for requirements for precast structural concrete (continued)
Compliance with BS EN 13369
[Ref 10.N]for the manufacturing
of the precast concrete element
outside the scope of a
designated precast concrete
product standard required
(where applicable)
Provide whether the precast
concrete element falling outside
the scope of a designated
precast concrete product
standard is to be manufactured
in accordance with BS EN
13369 [Ref 10.N], if different
from the default. Permitted
option limited to: yes, no
Only applies when the precast
concrete element is outside the
scope of a designated precast
concrete product standard.
The default is that a precast
concrete element that falls
outside the scope of a
designated precast concrete
product standard is
manufactured in accordance
with BS EN 13369 [Ref 10.N].
Given that BS EN 13670 [Ref
45.N]can cover the
manufacturing of precast
concrete elements not
conforming to any other precast
concrete standard, this design
output gives the flexibility to
specify, for a precast concrete
element that falls outside the
scope of a designated precast
concrete product, whether its
manufacturing needs to comply
with BS EN 13369 [Ref 10.N]or
not; however, specifying that a
precast concrete element does
not need to comply with BS EN
13369 [Ref 10.N] should only
be confined to minor site
manufactured elements of
limited structural significance.

Prestressing in the precast
concrete element required
Provide whether prestressing is
required for the precast
concrete element. Permitted
option limited to: yes, no.
This is derived from the design
and applies to both
pre-tensioning and
post-tensioning.
When prestressing is required
for a precast element it is
recommended that, as part of
the design documentation, a
range of alternative types and
positions of tendons is given
together with the criteria for
acceptance of alternatives,
including maximum assumed
prestressing losses. Equally it
is recommended that, in the
drawing(s)/model(s), the
required force before transfer
and its eccentricity is given and,
where the size and position of
the tendons are shown, it is
made clear whether the size
and position can vary and to
what extent.

construction with in-situ
concreting required
Provide whether the precast
concrete element is subject to
receive in-situ concrete on site
in composite precast/in-situ
construction. Permitted otpion
limited to: yes, no.
This is derived from the design,
and is most relevant for bridge
decks when an in-situ concrete
deck slab is cast on precast
concrete beams to form a deck.

Table C.58 Design outputs for requirements for precast structural concrete (continued)
Surface preparation required for
the precast concrete element
subject to receive in-situ
concrete on site in composite
precast-in situ construction
(where applicable)
Provide whether surface
preparation is required for the
precast concrete element
subject to receive in-situ
concrete on site in composite
precast/in-situ construction, if
different from the default.
Permitted option limited to: yes,
no.
Only applies when the precast
element is subject to receive
in-situ concrete on site in
composite precast/in-situ
construction.
The default is that surface
preparation is required to
provide a 'rough surface' to 6.2.
5 of BS EN 1992-1-1 [Ref
30.N], because the surface
roughness strongly influences
the interface shear between the
precast element and the in-situ
concrete. However, when
calculations in accordance with
6.2.5 of BS EN 1992-1-1 [Ref
30.N] show that, for a
non-prepared (i.e. smooth or
very smooth as defined in 6.2.5
of BS EN 1992-1-1 [Ref 30.N])
surface between concrete cast
at different times the interface
shear requirements are met,
then there is no need for the
surface to be prepared.
Rebates on precast concrete
bridge deck elements for
receiving permanent soffit
formwork required (where
applicable)
Provide whether rebates for
receiving permanent soffit
formwork are required to be
incorporated in the
manufacturing process for the
precast concrete bridge deck
element. Permitted option
limited to: yes, no.
Only applies when the precast
concrete element is a bridge
deck element.
The use of permanent soffit
formwork is common where an
in-situ concrete slab is cast over
precast concrete beams in a
bridge deck. In these cases,
and depending on the
layout/type of permanent soffit
formwork specified, the precast
beams may need to be
manufactured with rebates of
given layout and size to
accommodate the permanent
soffit formwork on site. When
rebates are required to be
incorporated in the
manufacturing process, the
details should be shown in
drawing(s)/model(s) for the
precast beams.

Appendix C. Design outputs for structural concrete
Precast concrete element
handling constraints
Describe any handling
constraints for the precast
concrete element.
Handling constraints to be
provided for the precast
concrete element and/or its part
include any constraints on the
minimum age for handling,
lifting and transport; on the
position of lifting/supporting
points during handling, lifting
and transport; on the position
and type of inserts for handling
and lifting; on methods of lifting
and type of lifting equipment; on
methods of transport; on
static/dynamic forces during
handling, lifting and transport;
on restraint during handling and
transport.
The handling constraints
specified for the precast
concrete element and/or its part
shall be shown and detailed in
the drawing(s)/model(s) and the
documentation referenced in
this Table.
Any lifting details provided as
part of the handling constraints,
to be subsequently used in the
preparation of a lifting scheme
at the construction stage, shall
be such that the lifting of the
precast concrete element can
be undertaken safely and
without any damage to the
element arising from the lifting
equipment. The minimum age
for handling, lifting and
transport is related to the
concrete strength development
and the need for the concrete to
be able to resist the stresses
induced during handling, lifting
and transport of the precast
concrete element without
permanent damage or
deformation.
In the provision of constraints
related to transport, it should be
noted that because of the layout
of trucks, it may not always be
possible to support precast
units beneath lifting points
during transport. Specific
provisions for restraint during
transport may be needed to
mitigate the risk of damage to
slim precast concrete element
flexing excessively vertically or
horizontally due to chafing,
oscillation, distortion of the
vehicle and centrifugal forces
d
i

Appendix C. Design outputs for structural concrete
Table C.59 Design outputs for handling and storage of precast concrete elements (continued)
Precast concrete element
storage constraints
Describe any storage
constraints for the precast
concrete element.
Storage constraints to be
provided for the precast
concrete element and/or its part
include any constraints on
supporting points during
storage; on maximum height of
a stack when stacking elements
vertically; on provisions to
maintain the stability of a stack.
The storage constraints are
intended to prevent induced
stresses, permanent distortion
and lack of fit of the precast
concrete elements, and should
be conducive to supporting
arrangements that minimise
settlements and deflections.
The storage constraints
specified for the precast
concrete element and/or its part
shall be shown and detailed in
the drawing(s)/model(s) and the
documentation referenced in
this Table.

Appendix C. Design outputs for structural concrete
Table C.60 Design outputs for placing and adjustment of precast concrete elements (continued)
Method of placing and
sequencing restrictions for
in-situ concrete in composite
precast/in-situ concrete
construction (where applicable)
Describe the sequencing and
restrictions of placing of the
in-situ concrete in composite
construction made of precast
concrete elements and in-situ
concrete.
Only applies when composite
precast/in-situ concrete
construction is used.
The sequencing and restrictions
of placing of the in-situ concrete
in composite construction
should be provided with the
objective of minimising
differential movement between
the precast concrete elements
during placing of the in-situ
concrete. In composite
precast/in-situ concrete bridge
decks, the design outputs
should require that the in-situ
concrete is placed in such a
sequence that the advancing
edge of the freshly placed
concrete over the full width of
the deck between any
longitudinal construction
joints is parallel to the deck
supports, and that the precast
beams are prevented from
moving laterally during the
placing of the in situ concrete;
this can prevent differential
movement between beams,
which may occur if the concrete
is placed in longitudinal strips,
and is particularly important
when the precast beams are
supported on flexible bearings.
The sequencing and restrictions
of placing specified shall be
shown and detailed in the
drawing(s)/model(s) and the
documentation referenced in
this Table.
Tolerance for the difference in
soffit level between adjacent
precast concrete bridge beams
in composite precast/in-situ
concrete construction (where
applicable)
Provide the allowable tolerance
for the difference in soffit level
between adjacent precast
concrete bridge beams in
composite precast/in-situ
concrete construction before
the in-situ concrete is placed, if
different from the default.
Provide value in mm.
Only applies when composite
precast/in-situ concrete bridge
deck construction is used with
adjacent precast concrete
beams with gaps of any length
between them.
The default allowable tolerance
is that the difference in soffit
level is within ± 5 mm of the
difference in soffit level between
adjacent beams shown in the
drawing(s)/model(s) for beams
up to 5 m in length, and within ±
10 mm for longer beams.

for the structural element and/or
its part.

provision of specific geometrical
tolerances for structural
concrete that are stricter than,
or additional to, the default
values; the default values of the
geometrical tolerances for
structural concrete are given in
Appendix I.
The provision of specific
geometrical tolerances different
from the default is rarely
necessary, but may be invoked
for aesthetic, durability and
fitting purposes or for special
structures. Where geometrical
tolerances different than the
default are specified, a review
of the implications on
constructability shall be
undertaken as part of the
design.
Whilst it is permitted to specify
geometrical tolerances for
structural concrete that are
stricter than, or additional to,
the default values, the default
values shall not be relaxed.

Appendix C. Design outputs for structural concrete
Table C.64 Design outputs for the frequency of trial panels for surface protection systems for
structural concrete
Design output / Reference
Information to be provided
as design outputs
Design requirements, advice or
notes for design outputs
The frequency of trial panels
for surface protection systems
for structural concrete
Provide the required frequency
of trial panels for surface
protection systems, if different
from the default.
The default frequency of trial
panels for surface protection
systems is once for each
permutation of different concrete
mixes, different surface finishes
and different orientations of the
structural element and/or its part
that the trial panels are
representing, no less than 56
days prior to the execution of the
permanent works.
Whether a frequency different
from the default should be
specified depends on project
specific requirements and the
type of surface protection
system(s). One trial panel for
each permutation might not
provide enough confidence in the
quality of the application of the
surface protection system where
aesthetic requirements are
particularity important for the
structural element and or its part.
Equally, one trial panel for each
permutation may not be enough
for anti-graffiti coatings, for which
successful graffiti removal needs
to be demonstrated in the trial.
The frequency specified may be
conditional; that is, the specified
number of trial panels to be
undertaken for each permutation
can be made subject to the
outcome from the initial set of trial
panels, by requiring additional
trial panels to undertaken only
upon unsatisfactory outcomes
from the initial set of trial panels.
The default of trial panels to be
undertaken no less than 56 days
prior to the execution of the
permanent works installation
should not be altered.
Where surface protection systems for structural concrete are required, the design outputs for trial
panels for surface protection systems for structural concrete shall be provided in accordance with Table
C.65.
Table C.65 Design outputs for trial panels for surface protection systems for structural concrete

00 mm in width may be

an example is where there is a

located within a sensitive area.

surface indentations or other
details that replicates the
structural element and/or its
part in the permanent works the
trial panel is representing. In
the absence of any specific
detail to be replicated by the
trial panel, a depth of 150 mm
should be specified.

Appendix C. Design outputs for structural concrete
Table C.66 Design outputs for site specific protective and control measures for the application
of hydrophobic impregnation (continued)
Site specific protective
measures requirements for the
application of hydrophobic
impregnation
Provide the requirements for
protective measures to be
implemented for the application
of hydrophobic impregnation to
the structural element and/or its
part subject to hydrophobic
impregnation and any
neighbouring affected features.
Hydrophobic impregnation
products can result in softening
effects and damage on
bearings, painted steel,
bituminous materials and joint
sealants, hence the need to
protect them during the
application of the product.
Hydrophobic impregnation
products result in a water
repellent surface, and if road or
railway surfaces are
contaminated with the product
this will result in a dangerously
slippery surface.
Protective measures to prevent
contamination of neighbouring
features from the hydrophobic
impregnation include
encapsulation, protective
sheeting and traffic
management. Traffic
management should be
specified as a protective
measure when working on
structures over or adjacent to
roads or railways. Further
advice on protective and control
measures that should be
provided for the application of
hydrophobic impregnation is
given in CD 373 [Ref 51.N].
Protective measures shall be
shown and detailed in the
drawing(s)/model(s) referenced
in this Table.

Downloaded from https://www.standardsforhighways.co.uk on 12-Nov-2025, CD 350 Version 1.0.0, published: 30-Sep-2025

======================================================================
CD 350 Version 1.0.0
Appendix C. Design outputs for structural concrete
Table C.66 Design outputs for site specific protective and control measures for the application
of hydrophobic impregnation (continued)
Non-continuous operation for
the application of hydrophobic
impregnation to the face of the
element permitted
Provide whether the application
of the hydrophobic
impregnation product to a face
of the structural element and/or
its part is permitted to be
undertaken in a non-continuous
operation. Permitted option
limited to: yes, no.
As a default, hydrophobic
impregnation should be
perfomed in a continuous
operation, to mitigate any risk of
the application not covering
completely the surface areas to
be impregnated. A
non-continuous operation for
the application of hydrophobic
impregnation shall only be
permitted to suit site specific
contraints and when specific
control measures are adopted.
Site specific constraints
includes cases where a
continuous operation would
result in excessively long work
patterns, for example a very
long edge beam or a large
abutment wall. Further advice
on site specific constraints to a
continuous operation for the
application of hydrophobic
impregnation is given in CD 373
[Ref 51.N].

Appendix D. Design outputs for structural steelwork
Appendix D. Design outputs for structural steelwork
D1
Design outputs for structural steelwork
Design outputs should be provided for the execution of structural steelwork in accordance with BS EN
1090-2 [Ref 46.N].
NOTE 1: BS EN 1090-2 [Ref 46.N] Annex A provides lists of the clauses for which:
1)
additional information is required;
2)
specifying additional requirements is permitted; and
3)
requirements are differentiated on the basis of execution class.
NOTE 2: Recommendations on additional information and requirements to be provided for the
execution of structural steelwork are given in PD 6705-2 [Ref 70.N] and should be followed as
implemented by CC 483 [Ref 92.N]
To supplement the fixed requirements in CC 483 [Ref 92.N], additional information and requirements
should be provided as design outputs for structural steelwork through:
1)
drawings / models that show the details of the structural steelwork; and
2)
documents that provide information about the structural steelwork.
The outputs from the design of structural steelwork should include details to define the following:
1)
the location, setting out, geometry, and tolerances of structural steelwork;
2)
constituent products and material requirements;
3)
identification of structural steel;
4)
joints and connections;
5)
surface treatment and preparation of steel substrates;
6)
support and articulation;
7)
assembly and erection, including the need for trial assemblies; and
8)
inspection, testing, and monitoring.
D2
Specific design outputs for structural steelwork
D2.1
Structural steelwork referencing
Each structure and component should be assigned a unique reference to enable cross referencing.
Where each structure is assigned a unique reference this should be consistent with the Overseeing
Organisation's asset management database.
D2.2
Basis of execution of structural steelwork
Details of the structural steelwork components that should be provided as follows:
1)
structure reference;
2)
component reference;
3)
drawing or model reference(s);
4)
document reference(s);
5)
Quantified Service Category(s) (QSC); and
6)
Execution Class.
The QSC for each structural steelwork detail should be selected from: F56, F71, F90, F120, or F140.
The QSC is to be clearly identified for all structures and components.
307

followed.
The execution class of structural steelwork should be selected from EXC1, EXC2, EXC3, EXC4, to
define the execution class of the component.
Note: Requirements in BS EN 1090-2 [Ref 46.N]and CC 483 [Ref 92.N] in some instances vary,
depending on Execution Class selected.
Component Specification "X" should be provided through the following information:
1)
structure reference;
2)
component reference; and
3)
Component Specification "X"
To define the code "X", the reference number should be designated CC483-mmm-yyyy:*ref*-*issue*,
where mmm-yyyy is the month and year of issue of this document, *ref* is the contract reference
number (not less than 3 characters) and *issue* is the issue number of the component specification.

provided in a list.
NOTE: BS EN 1090-2 [Ref 46.N] Annex A provides a list of the clauses subject to additional
information, options and requirements related to the execution classes.

Identification ( BS EN 1090-2 [Ref 46.N], 6.2)
The zones, for stainless steel, in which soft or low
stress stamps are not to be used for identification of
steel components.
Stamped, punched, or drilled marks may be
prohibited for stainless steel where visual or other
detriment to the surface finish is likely to occur.
This is relevant on fatigue-sensitive structures
where hard stamping would reduce the fatigue life.
Hard stamping is the best way of marking, but
ordinary stamps produce a detail category typically
of 56 or 63 (depending on the letter and its size).
Soft or low stress stamps give a better detail
category. Punched or drilled marks are acceptable.
Soft or low stress stamps are effectively detail
category 100, for fatigue assessment purposes
- see PD 6705-2 [Ref 70.N]

Appendix D. Design outputs for structural steelwork
Table D.1 Design outputs to be provided for the execution of structural steelwork (continued)
Assembly check ( BS EN 1090-2 [Ref 46.N], 6.1
0)
Requirements and extent of the trial assembly of
structural steelwork.
A full or staged trial assembly should be undertaken
where the designer identifies a requirement to prove
fit up between components and critical dimensions
especially where tolerances on overall geometry or
joint fit-up are small. This applies particularly to
bolted joints with butting faces.
A full or staged trial assembly of a superstructure
should be undertaken where any of the following
apply:
1) erection operations are to be undertaken within
restricted possession times;
2) construction is likely to be on the programme
critical path;
3) the vertical camber is critical to the correct dead
weight stress distribution in continuous main
girders, particularly in cable stayed or
suspension bridges; or
4) fit-up tolerances are small in latticed structures
which contain heavy members and rigid joints.
Where a full or staged trial assembly is required it
should comprise all steelwork, ancillary steelwork,
bearings and components, including those that may
affect site installation, all supported together in their
correct alignment and level.
Welding ( BS EN 1090-2 [Ref 46.N] Section 7)

General ( BS EN 1090-2 [Ref 46.N], 8.2.1)
Measures or means to secure the nuts of bolting

General ( BS EN 1090-2 [Ref 46.N], 8.2.1
Locations where welding of property class 4.6 nuts,
bolts, or washers is permitted.
Welding of property class 4.6 nuts, bolts and
washers should only be used where:
1) the QSC of the parent metal is not greater than
F36;
2) the welded component is not coated; and
3) neither the diameter of the bolt nor the thickness
of the parent metal is more than 12 mm.
Background information on welding of bolted joint
components is given in PD 6705-2 [Ref 70.N], C.17.
General ( BS EN 1090-2 [Ref 46.N], 8.2.1
Restrictions on orientation of bolting assemblies.
The orientation of bolting assemblies may be critical
for reasons of, for example, visual appearance,
corrosion resistance, accessibility of tools, and

General ( BS EN 1090-2 [Ref 46.N], 8.5.1)
Measures to limit the out-of-plane bending stiffness
of cover plates in the case of preloaded lap joints
subject to axial load acting in the plane of the friction
surfaces.
To achieve adequate contact between the friction
surfaces in preloaded lap joints, the out-of-plane
bending stiffness of cover plates should be limited.
This may be achieved by using two plates of half the
thickness each when the thickness of the original
cover plate exceeds the bolt size. The option to use
two cover plates of half the thickness in preloaded
lap joints may be permitted subject to conformance
to BS EN 1993-1-8 [Ref 32.N] unless there are other
design reasons why this should not be permitted. If
required by the designer, any measures permitted to
limit the out-of-plane bending stiffness of cover
plates should be provided.
Background information on fit up of preloaded bolted
joints is given in PD 6705-2 [Ref 70.N], C.18.

Appendix E. Design outputs for protection of steelwork ag...
Appendix E. Design outputs for protection of steelwork against corrosion
E1
Design output outcomes for protection of steelwork against corrosion
The design outputs for protection of steelwork against corrosion shall include:
1)
all details of the corrosion protection system to be applied;
2)
the standard of surface preparation;
3)
scheme-specific aesthetic requirements for the finish coat.
NOTE: Work-specific requirements for protection of steelwork against corrosion can be found in CC
486 [Ref 67.N] .
E1.1
Unique reference for protection of steelwork against corrosion
Each component or area of steelwork to receive corrosion protection, shall be assigned a unique
reference to enable cross-referencing.
Drawings or models shall be produced to clearly identify each component or area of steelwork to
receive corrosion protection.
For bridges, parapets, and other highway structures, except bearings and minor structures, the
structure should be subdivided into separate areas with unique area references to allow for variances in
characteristics.
All areas to which a unique reference applies shall only have a single category in accordance with
Table E.1 and identical characteristics such as environment, accessibility, and finish coat colour and
gloss level.
For bearings, the unique bearing reference shall be consistent with the design outputs produced in
accordance with Appendix H.
For minor structures, the unique minor structure reference shall be consistent with the design outputs
produced in accordance with CD 354 [Ref 18.N].
The structure name, structure reference, and structure location should be consistent with information
on the Overseeing Organisation's asset management database.
E2
Specific design outputs for protection of steelwork against corrosion
E2.1
Area description, environment, and accessibility
For all steelwork requiring protection against corrosion, except bearings and minor structures, the area
of steelwork subject to protection against corrosion shall be assigned an area description category in
accordance with Table E.1.
326
Downloaded from https://www.standardsforhighways.co.uk on 12-Nov-2025, CD 350 Version 1.0.0, published: 30-Sep-2025

Appendix E. Design outputs for protection of steelwork ag...
Table E.1 Applicability of area description categories
Area description category
Applicability
A
Exterior main surfaces, including shop welds.
B
Interior of box girder surfaces, except area C, but including shop
welds.
C
Friction surfaces of parent material at slip resistant connections.
D
Friction and outer surfaces of joint material at slip resistant
connections.
E
Exterior surfaces of site welds and weld affected areas.
F
Interior surfaces of site welds and weld affected areas.
G
All surfaces of parapets.
The environment within which steelwork requiring protection against corrosion is located shall be
defined as either Inland or Marine in accordance with Section 2 of CM 431 [Ref 54.N].
The accessibility of steelwork requiring protection against corrosion shall be defined as either Difficult
Access or Ready Access in accordance with Section 2 of CM 431 [Ref 54.N].
E2.2
Visually sensitive areas
Visually sensitive areas for protection of steelwork against corrosion shall be identified.
Visually sensitive areas of steelwork shall include the parts of a structure that are visible in the following
contexts:
1)
static views from and of major tourist attractions;
2)
views from and of very important national/international landscapes, cultural/historical sites (e.g.
National Parks, UNESCO World Heritage sites);
3)
views by users of nationally important public rights of way / recreational trails (e.g. national trails,
long distance footpaths);
4)
views by users of public open spaces for enjoyment of the countryside (e.g. country parks);
5)
static views from dense residential areas, longer transient views from designated public open
space, recreational areas;
6)
views from and of rare designated landscapes of national importance; and
7)
views from and of landscapes of regional importance.
Steelwork on structures that are defined as aesthetic category AC3 in CD 351 [Ref 102.N] shall be
classed as visually sensitive, unless the steelwork cannot be viewed from a public space.
NOTE: Where available, the structure-specific Aesthetic Appraisal Documents, in accordance with CD
351 [Ref 102.N], provide further guidance on whether the structure, or parts thereof, are considered
visually sensitive.
The following shall be provided for each visually sensitive area of maintenance painting:
1)
a unique reference for the visually sensitive area;
2)
the unique area references of the areas of maintenance painting that are included in the visually
sensitive area;
3)
a description including the extents of the area and reasons for being visually sensitive; and
4)
aesthetic requirements.
327
Downloaded from https://www.standardsforhighways.co.uk on 12-Nov-2025, CD 350 Version 1.0.0, published: 30-Sep-2025

PAGE 329 of 417
======================================================================
CD 350 Version 1.0.0
Appendix E. Design outputs for protection of steelwork ag...
Where required for visually sensitive areas, additional requirements for light intensity at the workface
and paint quality verification shall be provided.
The light intensity at the workface may be increased above the default of 500 lux over 1 m2.
The frequency of measurement of the gloss level of the finished paint system may be increased above
the default of once for every 10 m2, up to once for every 1 m2.
The frequency of visual comparison of the colour of the finished paint system with the painted tinplate
reference panel may be increased above the default of once for every 10 m2, up to once for every 1 m2.
The frequency of testing of paint coats for pin-holing and porosity may be increased above the default
of once for each area covering a minimum of 20% of that area.
NOTE: The defaults for light intensity, frequency of measurement of the gloss level, frequency of visual
comparison of the colour and frequency of testing for pin-holing and porosity are as specified in CC 486
[Ref 67.N].
E2.3
Corrosion protection design
E2.3.1
Substrate cleaning
The cleaning of steelwork during surface preparation shall be in accordance with Section 4 of CM 431
[Ref 54.N].
Wet cleaning on site shall be used by default.
NOTE: The default for wet cleaning is as specified in CC 486 [Ref 67.N].
Where cleaning solvents other than water are required, the locations for and requirements on their use
shall be provided.
NOTE: In most cases, the use of a cleaning agent followed by rinsing is considered to be more effective
than the use of a cleaning solvent.
The use of cleaning solvents may be permitted where the presence of oil, grease, or significant
amounts of soluble salts are anticipated.
Note: Significant amount of soluble salts are concentrations above 40 mg/m2.
E2.3.2
Stripe coats
The need for stripe coats shall be in accordance with Section 4 of CM 431 [Ref 54.N] .
E2.3.3
Finish coats
The aesthetic requirements for finish coats shall be in accordance with Section 4 of CM 431 [Ref 54.N].
E2.3.4
Hot-dip galvanising
Hot dip galvanised coatings shall meet the requirements of BS EN ISO 1461 [Ref 50.N] as the default ,
unless otherwise agreed with the Overseeing Organisation.
NOTE: The default for hot dip galvanised coatings is as specified in CC 486 [Ref 67.N] .
The requirements for hot-dip galvanised coatings in BS EN ISO 1461 [Ref 50.N] shall only be changed
in exceptional circumstances, where specialist technical advice has been sought.
The thickness of the hot-dip galvanised coating, where greater than that given in BS EN ISO 1461 [Ref
50.N], shall be provided.
Where the thickness of the hot-dip galvanised coating is greater than that given in BS EN ISO 1461
[Ref 50.N], the requirements for surface preparation for hot-dip galvanising, shall be provided.
E2.3.5
Protective systems for minor structures
In defining the extents of the ground sections for minor structures, the nominal ground level shall be
identified.
328
Downloaded from https://www.standardsforhighways.co.uk on 12-Nov-2025, CD 350 Version 1.0.0, published: 30-Sep-2025



======================================================================
PAGE 330 of 417
======================================================================
CD 350 Version 1.0.0
Appendix E. Design outputs for protection of steelwork ag...
NOTE: The default nominal ground level, as specified in CC 486 [Ref 67.N], is 600 mm below the door
opening.
Where a different nominal ground level is required, this shall be provided along with the columns /
masts to which it applies.
E2.3.6
Corrosion protection of fasteners in steelwork
Fasteners shall be protected against corrosion.
Details of protective coatings with which fasteners are supplied shall be provided, where different to the
defaults.
NOTE 1 : The default for protective coatings with which the fasteners are supplied is as specified in CC
486 [Ref 67.N] .
NOTE 2 : Stainless-steel fasteners do not need to be supplied with a protective coating.
Other than for stainless-steel fasteners, alternatives to the default shall not be provided unless agreed
with the Overseeing Organisation.
NOTE 3: The default for protective coatings with which the fasteners are supplied is as specified in CC
486 [Ref 67.N].
E2.3.7
Treatment of fasteners in steelwork prior to assembly
Prior to assembly, fasteners shall be treated with, or in preparation for, the required corrosion protection
system.
Details of treatments to fasteners shall be provided, where different to the defaults.
NOTE: The defaults for treatments of fasteners is as specified in CC 486 [Ref 67.N] .
Stainless-steel fasteners may need painting for aesthetic reasons.
Fasteners shall not be treated with thermal metal spraying.
NOTE 1 : Metal coatings for fasteners are hot-dipped galvanized, zinc electroplating and sherardizing.
NOTE 2 : Hot-dipped galvanizing applied before assembly provides long term protection.
NOTE 3 : Zinc electropainting and sherardizing applied before assembly only provide short-term
protection and could need a full protective paint system.
E2.3.8
Treatment of fasteners in steelwork after assembly
After assembly on site, uncoated and temporarily coated fasteners shall be prepared for painting by
blast cleaning.
Note: Medium profile is the default surface roughness of fasteners following blast cleaning specified in
CC 486 [Ref 67.N].
Where a surface profile other than medium is required, either fine or coarse profile in accordance with
BS EN ISO 8503-1 [Ref 66.N] shall be provided.
E2.3.9
Corrosion protection of connections before assembly
Preloaded connections where paint is the only required coating shall be protected from corrosion
through application of the first coat of paint.
The requirements for the first coat of paint, where different to the default shall be provided.
NOTE 1: Default requirement for the first coat of paint is as specified in CC 486 [Ref 67.N] .
NOTE 2: For slipresistant connections, the standard of preparation and treatment of the friction
surfaces of joint material and parent material is provided in CC 483 [Ref 92.N], in accordance with
Appendix D of this document.
329
Downloaded from https://www.standardsforhighways.co.uk on 12-Nov-2025, CD 350 Version 1.0.0, published: 30-Sep-2025



======================================================================
PAGE 331 of 417
======================================================================
CD 350 Version 1.0.0
Appendix E. Design outputs for protection of steelwork ag...
Paints other than a primer or sealer shall not be taken into the contact surface area for slip-resistant
connections.
NOTE: Preloaded connections that are not required to be slip-resistant are covered in BS EN 1090-2
[Ref 46.N], F.4 and in CC 483 [Ref 92.N].
Non preloaded connections where paint is the only required coating shall be protected from corrosion
through application of the paint system to the joint surfaces.
The requirements for the paint system to non-preloaded connections, where different to the default
shall be provided.
NOTE: The default requirements for the paint system to non-preloaded connections are specified in CC
486 [Ref 67.N].
Where application of the full paint system to the joint surfaces of non- preloaded connections is not
required, at least the primer and first undercoat shall be applied.
Joint surfaces may not require the full paint system where the final coat is to be applied to the adjacent
steelwork on site.
E2.3.10
Paint application
The method of paint application shall be consistent with the type of paint.
NOTE: The default methods of paint application, as specified in CC 486 [Ref 67.N], are brush, airless
spray, and airassisted spray.
The use of one of the default application methods may be prohibited due to environmental or local
restrictions.
NOTE: Paints and other protective coatings in the Manual of Paints for Structural Steelwork in CG 303
[Ref 68.N] are applied either by brush or airless spray or by both. However, for paints with lower
viscosity, for example, aluminium epoxy sealer, use can be made of air-assisted spray equipment to
avoid over application, flooding, and overspray of paint.
Paint rollers shall not be used.
NOTE: Paint application using rollers has been found to provide unsatisfactory outcomes.
Maximum overcoating times where different to the following defaults shall be provided:
1)
primers not exposed outside: within 8 weeks of their application;
2)
primers applied in the workshop and exposed outside for any period following their application:
within 2 weeks of their application;
3)
primers applied on site: within 72 hours of their application;
4)
all intermediate undercoats: within 72 hours of their application; and
5)
finish coats: within 7 days.
NOTE: The defaults for maximum overcoating times are as specified in CC 486 [Ref 67.N] .
E2.3.11
Procedure trials
The 'reference areas ' shall be used for procedure trials as defined in Annex A of BS EN ISO 12944-7
[Ref 57.N].
Procedure trials shall be identified through the unique 'Area reference ' along with a description of the
specific elements to be used.
The areas to be used in the procedure trials shall be selected to represent details, components or
areas at greater risk of the surface preparation or paint application not being executed correctly, such
as fixings, bearings, joints, or areas where access is constrained.
